Institutional Network
Education - orphanage
Abstract: AFSt- Ausführliche Beschreibung verschiedener karitativer Einrichtungen in Amsterdam, wie das Diakonische Waisenhaus, das Bürger-Waisenhaus, das Almoseniers-Waisenhaus, das Wallonische Waisenhaus, das Mennonitische Waisenhaus, das Frauenhaus, das Pesthaus und der Hortus Medicus.
Notes: I did 
not start at the beginnning of this document; it is a report on 
the charitable institutions in Amsterdam written probably either 
for Neubauer's trip to Amsterdam in 1697 or Francke's trip in 
1705. I began on frame 586 with the description of the Mennonite
Orphanage.

Mennoniste Wees-huys

Dit Weeshuys Staat op de nieuwe Prinse Gracht, t'usschen de bysel
straat en Reguliers Gracht; en is gesticht in den Jaare 1676 van 
de Vlaamingen en Waterlanders, naamen daan by deese Secte gekent,
en van andere Secten en Mennonisten, die veelerley zyn 
onderscheyden worden; ende de Kinderen zyn Anno 1677 daar inne 
gebragt.

Den ingak ofte Deur op de Prinse Gracht, staat int midden, waar 
door men intreet. ten eersten siet men een Armen Bosch hangen, 
daan booven men deese vaarsen leest:

Deelt milt een Aalmoes uyt, die hier komt in getreden;
Gy kunt noogt uw Geschenk, met beeten vrucht besteden:
Want hoe wort d'Armoe, ooit onnooselder geleen,
Als Ouderloos te zyn, en weereloos met een!

Ter slinker hand eenige treeden opgaande, hiet men de Eecsaal en 
school voor de Meyskes, gelyk ten rechter hand voon de Jongens: 
En daan boven de Slaap-plaatsen van de Jonens en Meyskens; ook de
buyten-vaders en buytenmoeders Kamer ter weersyde. Op de darde 
verdieping is het Naay-School van de Meysyes: als mede de 
Sieken-kamers van de Jongens en Meysjes. Daar booven op de 
vierde verdieping zyn de Kleersolders Kleer-kamers, etc. En op de
vysde verdieping staan de getouwen, daar de Jongens in de Weevery
geoesfent worden.

Diese Vlaamingen en Waaterlanders hebben mede een 
oude-Vrouwen-huys voor aan in de Elends-Straat, daar in de 20 
Oude Vrouwen worden onderhouden, deselve worden alle aan eene 
Tafel gelykerhand gespyst.

In't gemelde Weeshuys zuy ook de Wooningen van de binne Valdre en
binne-Moeders; Twee speel-plaatsen, een vor de Jongens en een 
voor de Meysjens. Oover de Tuyn die seer groot is, teogende 
kerk-straat aan, siet men de Backery, en een Bry-school voor de 
kleene Kinderen.

Alles is seen ordentelyk in dit huys verdeele, en ? den daaar in 
40 Jongens en 42 Meysjens in all Seedigheyd wel op gevoeder en 
gekleed; met goede Spyse en order opgebragt en onderhouden, tot 
verwondering van de geene die het besichtigen.

NOTE: each of these descriptions gives the entire history of the
institution! Some go back as far as the 14th and 15th centuries.
This is a fascinating set of documents!
Research Notes: AMF 5/21/2025
I believe this is SBB-F_28_2_1, the information seems to match with that in Groeschl's Stabi Metadata.

Death
Abstract: Heusch Abrahamssohn hat Medikamente aus der Apotheke des Waisenhauses Halle erhalten. Abstract: AFSt- Benson dankt Francke für die in Halle erwiesene Freundlichkeit und Fürsorge.
Notes: Engeland
Most reverend Sr.
Having so good an opertunity I thought it my Duty to trouble you 
with these few lines, and hereby, to thank you for your 
perticular love, care and kindness shown to me when I was at 
Halle, of which I hope always to have a gratefull membrance, and 
shall always be ready, if I could be honoured with doing you Sr. 
any servise, which is, and always as I shall acknowledge, my 
Duty. Wishing you, then Sr with your worthy Lady, to whom I give
my humble servise all happiness and prosperity, I remain Worthy 
Sr your most obliged & dutifull servant,
Harry Benson
October 30th 1710

Sr. Understanding by Mr. Mackbeth that there is a want of a 
supply of money for our Young Pupils I desire therefore that you 
will send a letter to my Brother Mr. ? Hoare at Mr. ? Greves 
Mercht in Hambourgh for to remitt you the vallue of Twenty POunds
Sterling & after Xmas I desire a particular acct. of these 
expences may be sent to Sr. Your most humb. serv. ? Hoare.

Education - pedagogy
Education - student life
Economic network
Goods - cloth
Theology
Abstract: AFSt- Benson empfiehlt seinen Sohn Harry, der nach dem Schulbesuch in Halle den Beruf eines Kaufmanns ergreifen soll.
Notes: Instructions to be observed in ye tutoridge of Harry Benson

1. He shall be above all well grounded in ye principles of ye 
Christian Religion, not ingaged in any POints of Controversie & 
nothing in opposition to ye Doctrine of ye Church of England.

2. In ye French, Latin & German tongues is it in his Friends 
desire to have him perfected, & especially, that in the Latin & 
German tongues his tutor shall instruct him.

3. He shall apply himself to his writing & Arithmetik after ye 
English manner

4. He shall be taught something of ye Mathematicks, especially 
Geography, with ye use of Globes.

5. His tutor shall buy for him his waring, Apparell etc. & all 
the Expences for it, with the other yt are necessary for Masters 
& farther Instructing, shall he charge together to an exact 
Account, to send over the same every half year.

6. With all necessaries he shall be supplied, but nothing 
farther.

7. He shall be allowed after ye rate of 5 shillings english p. 
month for his Pocket-Expences, but also instructed in a frugall 
way of living.

8. He shall be as little out of ye eyes of his Tutors as 
possible, especially at ye times, yt is allowed for diverting 
himself & going abroad.

10. When the stock of money is near out, shall Mr. Hoar be 
informed of it, that he may take timely care to supply him before
he want it.

Antoher Extract out of the Instruction given to Mr. Jacobi by Mr 
Hoar.

I would have you acquaint his Tutor, that it is in his Friends 
directions, that he lye in the same room with him, & keep him 
close to his studies, which will be to perfect him in his Latin &
French tongues, & that he sees yt he according to ye Method of ye
Books, he has with him, practices et improves in writing & 
Arithmetick. He must likewise learn ye Mathematick & ye use of 
Globes & Geography. His Tutor must likewise buy all his 
Cloathes, which are desired not be fine, but plane and neat, and 
to be as furgall for him in Expences as may be, and to be sure, 
that he is a strict observer of ye Sabbath Day, not idling away 
no part of it, but go with him constantly to ye publick service 
of ye Church, and afterwards to examine, what he has heard. If 
Mr. Mackbeth has ye use of devotions with ye children in their 
Chamber, I give my Consent, yt he may be present at them. But I 
desire, that he will take all otehr opportunities of instructing 
him in ye Principles of ye Christian Religion, but not in any 
doctrine that is contrary to that of ye CHurch of England. I 
desire, yt he not will let him go upon any diversions without his
being with him, & yt he will improve all those diversion to his 
souls good. his Tutor is desired to keep an exact Account, of 
what he layes out for him, and send it to me every half years, 
and also how my Brother behaves himself, and what progress he 
makes in his studies. He will find my Brother to be of a temper,
easie with good words to be won upon. He is apt to be to hasty 
in his Speech & speeks before he thinks, which his Tutor to 
remedy must take care. His temper is, yt he loves not long to be
kept to one study, and therefore, when he is tired of one, let 
him enter upon another, but not to suffer him to idle away his 
time, but to make the best Improvement of it. Let his Company be
such as he can improve himself by in ye ways of Virtue and Piety,
and let his Tutor allways take Mr. Francks Directions, as to 
Management of him, and to write me, when his money is near out, 
that i may ordre more etc. etc.

Custom 1: 1708-07-12
Custom 2: 51.507351, -0.127758
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Custom 4: SBB-F_30_2_3
Custom 7: Benson, Harry
Keywords: <lang>English</lang>
<religion>Pietist</religion>
Notes: London,
July ye 12th 1708
Sr.
By ye Recommendation of Severall friends and Acquaintances I send
my Sonn Harry ye Bearer hereof to you, & I desire you will take 
particular care of him in his Education & Learning I intend him 
for a marcht & therefore desire his Learning may be to yt purpose
he has Learnt French for some years. Yt I question not but he 
will be soone perfect in yt. If it pleases God he has his health
and as I hear he proceeds in Learning he shall stay ye longer 
with you, I mutch hear of ye dilligence and Carefulnes in yr 
Schools, and I have no reason to question but you will be as kind
to, and careful of my sonn as any other you Knowing his good 
Education is the best thing can be done for him, you will not let
him forgett his duty to Allmighty God, is the cheef thing I 
recommend to you then I am sure he will every way prosper & I 
wish you ye same in all ye concerns, & if anything hapens I can 
serve you in hear, I shall be very reddy & commending you to ye 
blessing & protection of God concludes in yr friend & servt Wm 
Benson

Notes: Westminster, 12 Decemb. 99?
Honor'd Sr.
By the Directions of the Honorable Society for propogating 
Christian Knowledge (who have chosen me their secretary for 
Corresdpondences, & of whom I suppose you have formerly had some 
Account from Mr. Wigers & Mr. Mehder, I am to acquaint you that 
they desire to maintain a Frequent Intelligence with you, both to
be in formed of the great things you have already don in Germany 
towards the promoting God's Glory & the spreading of Christian 
Knowledge +tc, and also to communicate to you what measures they 
take in the carrying on of the same Designs etc.
 
I am also particularly desired by our good Dr. Bray to tell you 
that he is upon the point of going into the West Indies where he 
desires to settle a strict Correspondence with you & that both 
your Letters & his may pass thro my hands & that in the meant 
time you be pleas'd to Accept of the small present he has made 
you of his Books, videlicet. 1. Lectures upon the 
Church-Catechism fol. 2 A Discourse upon the Baptismal Covenant. 
3. Apostolick Charity. 4. Bibliotheca Catechetica. The other 
papers are writ by a most excellent Minister named Frank, a 
Member of our Society. My Fathers book, and the Bishop of 
Gloucesters Sermon I desire you to receive from me as a small 
Acknowledgement of the Great Respect which shall be ever paid you
by 
Honor'd Sr.
your most Devoted Servant
John Chamberlayne

if you can understand my English sr. I shall very easily 
understand your High Dutch. The above mention'd Books are sent 
to Mr. David Otte Merchant near the Niclaus Kirk Hamburg.

Reference Type:  Generic
Record Number: 117
Author: Chamberlayne, John
Year: 1700
Title: Petty France, 
Westminster
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1700/06/28
Type of Work: Letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/11:3 [10212]
England Fasc XXVI, s. 841/56; Halle: 30, 28; film nr. 21, 323
Custom 1: 1700-06-28
Custom 2: 51.499580, -0.135600
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Keywords: Chamberlayne John
Westminster
SPCK
Chamberlin
Francke A H
Halle
Notes: Petty France Westminster
28 June 1700

Revd. Sir
The Society which has formed itself in this City for the 
Propogation of Christian Knowledge have rec'd great Satisfaction 
from the readiness you have shown to be one of their Members & to
keep a Correspondence wth them. And they trust in God that you 
will prove a very usefull instrument in promoting yt great work 
in wch they are engaged.

You have in their former Letter been acquainted with the three 
main Branches of their design, The Education of Poor Children in 
this Kingdom, The Spreading of Christianity in ye Plantations, 
And the reclaiming of those among us who entertain opinions 
inconsistent wth the Fundamentalls of our holy Religion.

The first Step to these excellent Ends they conceive will be to 
engage ye Clergy to meet frequently together to consider of the 
most rpoper means to carry on these pious disigns and to order 
their Meetings so that they may give no offence to others nor any
just occasion of Reflection on themselves That ye Leave & 
Direction of ye Diocesan be desired, That the Laws of ye Land & 
Canons of ye Church be their Rule, THat the place of Meeting be, 
if possible, a privat house & the Manner Such as may be most 
reputable to ye Clergy. & mayy convince ye World that they are 
carrying on the work of their great Master, The Salvation of the
Soulds of Men. Now this ye Society must leave to ye Discretion 
of their Reverend Brothren according to their different 
Circumstances, only they earnestly desire of you that you would 
use yor utmost Endeavours to engage as many of the Clergy as 
possibly you can to meet together at such certai times & places &
in such numbers as shall be thought most convenient. And they 
are in great hopes yt you will Succeed in this matter since it is
what is particularly recommended by the Arch Bishop of 
Canterbury, & others ye Lords Y Bps in their Circular Letter in 
April 1699.

When such meetings as these are formed they hope that ye first 
care of ye Clergy will be to encourage & direct each other in ye 
Severall Branches of their own Duty since the faithfull discharge
of all ye Parts of ye Ministeriall care is the ordinary means 
that God has enjoyned for the preservering & propagating 
CHristianity and The regulating the Lives of those who profess 
it.

Next to this they most heartily recommend a zealous Application 
of the Clergy to those of their Parishioners who are of Ability 
especially Magistrates to assist them in such meetings & that 
they would subscribe liberally toward the setting up of Schools 
for poor Children, to instruct them in ye Principles of ye 
Christian Religion & fitt them for Employments, wch is ye most 
probable method of making them sound members of the Chruch & 
usefull ones of the State.

They have herewith sent you an Acct of ye Modell of Ye Meetings 
of the Clergy in Bedford & Buckinghamshires together wth the 
Methods ye Society has taken in raising subscriptions and 
regulating the schools wch they have already sett up in & about 
London, wch possibly may be usefull to you in your deliberations 
about the same things in the Country.

They desire you would from time to time give them Information of 
what progress is made in these matters, & that you would direct 
yor Letters to me whom they have made Secretary of the Society, 
by whose hands they shall communicate what they shall have 
hereafter to offer to you and what you shall request from them.

They beg yor constant Prayers to Almighty God that he wouldassist
them in their deliberations, & prosper them in yor endeavours 
they use to propate true Christian Knowledge in ye World; And 
they do assure you of their joynt intercession to the Thorne of 
Grace for the same Blessing on yourself, and the rest of our 
Brethren

I am Reverend Sr
Your most humble Servant
John Chamberlayne
By order of the society

Author: Chamberlayne, John

Title: Petty-France, 
Westminster
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1700/06/28
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/11:2 [10211]
England Fasc XXVI, s. 841/56; Halle: 30, 28; film nr. 21, 321
Custom 1: 1700-06-28
Custom 2: 51.499580, -0.135600
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Keywords: Chamberlayne John
Francke A H
Westminster
Chamberlin
Halle
SPCK
London
Notes: Petty France, Westminster
28 June 1700
Rev. Sr

The visible decay of Religion in this Kingdon, wch the monstrous 
increase of Deism, Prophaness, and vie, has excited the zeal of 
several Persons of the best Character in ye Cities of London and 
Westminster, and other parts of the Nation to associate 
themselves in order to consult together, how to put a stop to so 
fatal an Inundation. The cause thereof they believe in great 
measure to arise from ye barbarous Ignorance, observable among ye
common People especially of those of ye poorer sort, & this to 
proceed from want of due care in ye Education of ye Youth, who if
early Instructed in ye Principles of true Religion & seasoned wth
ye Knowledge of God, & a just concern for their everlasting 
welfare, could not possibly (wth the ordinary assistance of Gods 
good Spirit) degenerate into such vile & unchrstian practices, as
they now generally do. To rememdy these Evils wch cry aloud to 
Heaven for vengeance, they agreed to use their best Interest & 
Endeavours to incline ye Hearts of Generous & well disposed 
Persons, to contribute towards ye Erecting of Schools in those 
Cities & ye parts adjacent, for ye Instruction of such poor 
Children in Reading, Writing & Catechism, whose Parents or 
Relations are not able to afford them ye ordinary means of 
Education: and as they look upon this to be ye most effectual 
method to train up ye poorer sort in sobriety and ye Knowledge of
Christian Principles, so they assure themselves yt the good 
effects wch may be wrought thereby will prove a powerfull argumt 
to engage others in better circumstances to make so necessary a 
Provision for their Children

The success of this Undertaking (whereby the Education of between
five and six hundred poor children is already taken care for) 
encourages them to hope yt if the like Industry & Application 
were observed in ye other parts of this Kingdom ye Children & 
Youth might be universally well principled and ye growing 
Gerneration make a Conscience of fearing God, and these hopes 
have induced them to use their utmost Endeavours to prevail with 
all pious & well inclined Christians in ye several parts of ye 
nation, to joyn their Hearts & purses in advancing to perfection 
so excellent and glorious a work.

A farther branch of their Design is, to carry on ye measures of 
late happily begun for ye Propagating of Christian Knowledge in 
ye Plantations: The Progress herein made appears by ye Noble 
Provision of Books for ye Clergy in those Parts, whereof ye world
has had already an acct. in Print and that so Blessed work may 
not fail of being prosperous & successfull, they are taking care 
to solicit Benefactions for the Supplying from time to time, 
whatsoever shall be wanting to accomplish it. the third branch 
of their Design is to bring those poor deluded People to true 
notions of Christianity, who either expressly deny or know very 
little of ye great & fundamental Doctrines of our most holy 
Religion, those especially, wch relate to a Crucified Saviour 
etc.

The particular steps taken for ye effecting a work so acceptable 
to Almighty God, and so exceeding beneficial to ye Souls of 
Mankind, they will be ready hereafter to acct for, as they find 
Persons inclined to encourage & assist them.

These are ye means of Promoting Christian Knowledge, which 
through ye assistance of Almight God they trust, may in some 
degree retreive Ye decays of PIety among us, & cause ye power of 
the Gospel to appear to ye unconverted.

the Request they make you, is that, as a Minister of Jesus Christ
and a Lover of Souls (which Character they have rec'd of you) you
would joyn wth them in ye prosecution? of these their pious 
Intentions, in such methods as ye Laws of ye Land & Canons of ye 
Church do recomend; and according to such prudent means as they 
shall from time to time joyntly agree upon. In full perswasion 
hereof, and that they may create in you a Mutuall confidence with
respect to them they have nominated you a Member of their 
Society, and desire to maintain a Correspondence wth you, and 
accordingly, So soon as you shall signifie your appropbation, 
they will give you Speedy notice in what manner and by what hands
to carry on such Correspondence. the Society have enjoyned me to
signifie unto you these Particulars and therefore Intreat you to 
direct your answer to me, who am,
Revd. Sr.
Your most Humble Servant
John Chamberlayne

Ludolf Mr
Notes: Westminster, 29 July 1701
Reverend Sr

I don't question but the Worthy Mr. Ludolf, Dr. Mecken, Mr. 
Wigers or Mehder do from time to time give you a particular 
Account of the great & good Designs that are carrying on in all 
parts of England for the Promoting the Glory of God, & the 
enlarging of the Knowledge & Practice of the Holy Gospel, to this
end it has pleased our Gracious King to make us a BodyPolitic as 
you will see by the Inclosed Copy of our Printed Charter to which
Ir efer you --- The rest of the Papers which I take the 
opportunity of sending you by the Bearer will give you a farther 
Light into the Affaires of the Society, who are engaged in a gr 
good Works of several Kinds but the Business of Charity Schools 
is there Darling Employment it being of all others of the 
greatest Importance because it tends directly to a 
Gerneral-Reformation of all the Poor Children throughout the 
Nation for whom both Spiritual as well as Temporall Provision has
been too long & too much neglected, however blessed be God you 
will find by the Inclosed account that a very great deal has been
done for them especially in London & Westminster considering how 
lately we have begun upon that Head ---- I must not omitt telling
you that that one Design has heard so well abroad that the 
Reverend Mr. Scherer our Correspondent for St. Gall in 
Swisserland has engaged the Gouvernors of that little Republic to
make a public Degree about the Institution of Youth whereof I 
transmit you a Copy -- The Reverend Mr. Ostervald Minister of 
Nufchatel, & author of that Incomparable Piece, called Les 
Sources de la Corruption queregne parmy les Cretiens etc. has 
engaged the Clergy of that Government into the like measures & in
a Strict Correspondence with our Society, the same I doubt not 
will be shortly done in Zurich, Basil, Bearn, Geneva, & in some 
parts of HOlland, Utrecht etc. where we have already begun a 
Correspondence -- of the Promoting Christ's Kingdome by these & 
other Methods. I could give you most Joyfll accounts from the 
Remotest parts of the Earth, particularly from several of our 
Colonies in the West Indies, North America, but I will defer it 
till another opportunity being also not without hopes of Inducing
that Excellent man your amesake Mr. Franke of Bedfordshire to 
draw up a large & particular account of what has been done 
directly by our Society itself since it has been Erected & also 
by the Influence it has had upon other Societies which have been 
the Product & offspring thereof.

You know Sr. there is no such effectual spur to Mankind as 
Example, therefore when It has been told in Germany what their 
Protestant Brethren are doing In England, I don't doubt but a 
virtuous emulation of equalling or excelling us will be stir'd up
in the Hearts of the good men in your Country, and then that the 
grace & Blessings of ye Almighty (who only gives the Increase) 
may be pour'd down without measure o their Religious Endeavors 
are the most Fervent and Daily prayers of Rev. Sr.
Your most Humble Servant
John Chamberlayne, Secretary

Notes: Westminster, Easter Sunday, 24 April 1709

Reverend Sr.

I should never Forgive myself if I let slip such an opportunity 
of Sc? you & informing myself of the State of your Health etc. as
is now given me by my worthy Friend Mr. Behme, & late fellow 
servant under the best of Masters Prince George of Denmark; who 
will acquaint you how well known you and your Pious labors (so 
signelly blest by Divine Providence) and how very Dear they are 
to all Good Men in the several Religious Societies lately 
erected, & abt to be Erected both in S & N. Britain; to him 
therefore I refer you for the particulars thereof, & so I do for 
the more Minute Accounts of all our Designs (having freely put 
our Mss. Journals, Letters &tc. into his hands for that purpose) 
& that I may not rob you of too much of your Precious time, I 
conclude these few lines with my HEarty Prayers that God wil 
continue to Pour down his Blessings on your School & Wees-haus, &
that Mr. Frank may live to see it so firmly established that the 
gates of Hell may never Prevail against it. I am with great 
sincereity & respect, your most humble servant, John Chamberlayne

I have sent you a few of those Books & Papers published by our 
society & pray that we from time to time mutually impart to each 
other all the good things that Promote God's glory, etc.

Notes: this letter is in French -- did not 
transcribe
description from finding aid:
Chamberlain schickt mehrere Exemplare eines neuen, sich im Druck 
befindlichen Martyrologiums in französischer übersetzung,
in dem ein [nicht genannter] Autor die Leiden der Protestanten 
unter dem Papismus schildert. Er bittet Francke, dem Autor 
Informationen über ihm bekannte Protestantenverfolgungen 
zukommen zu lassen. Falls Francke es wünsche, könne sein
Bericht unter seinem eigenen Namen in das Werk aufgenommen 
werden. Ferner bittet er, Francke möge Subskribenten für
das Werk gewinnen. Er entschuldigt die Hast, mit der die 
französische übersetzung angefertigt wurde. 
Abschließend bittet er, der Adressat möge seine das Werk 
betreffenden Mitteilungen nicht mit der anderen Post für die 
SPCK schicken. Außerdem sendet er Francke einen Bericht zu 
übertritten katholischer Iren zum Protestantismus.

Keywords: Chamberlayne

Notes: Pety France, Westminster
24 Nov. 1712
Reverend & Dear Sr

In the name of the Reverend Dr. Bray , the Author of the 
Martyrology & in my own, I return you many Thanks for your last 
kind letter, which I should acknowledge more particularly & 
answer Paragraphically if I had not left the sd Letter in the 
hands fo the sd Reverend Dr.; I shal do that therefore by some 
other opportunity in the mean time I could not let our Pious 
Missionary part heance (I call him ours, because the society to 
which I belong, & because I myself claim so great a share in him)
I say I could not let this good man depart without Saluting you, 
wihtout answering you that I offer up my most Hearty Prayers to 
God that he would continue to Bless & Prosper as he has hitherto 
do in a wonderful Manner, all the Great Designs you are engaged 
in, for the Glory of God & the Good of Souls; 

Sr having been inform'd by the Reverend Mr. Plutscho the Bearer 
that you are going to print the N. Testament in Malabaric I beg 
leave to suggest to you whether it would not be doubly usefull to
the Peoples in India if the Portuguese (as spoken in those parts 
were also printed ccolumnwise in the smae Book in the manner you 
have don the sd N. Testament in Vulgar learned greek; by which 
means those that understand only one of those Languages may learn
the other from thence, for I count that by the help of one or 
tother of those Tongues that book may be spread with great 
?cation throughout the Indys.

Sr. I have one thing more to say to you, and then I shal ease you
of the preset Trouble. Mr. Plutscho has taken the Charge upon 
him of Carrying 2 or 3 Books from me to Dr. Ludwig of Leipsic, if
he should go no nearer than Hall, I beg you to send them forward 
by some secure hand, because it is of great Consequence to Rev. &
Dear Sr. , your most Humble servant,
John Chamberlayne

Notes: London 7th July 1716
Sr
I take this occasion to salute you wth my most sincere respects, 
and to thank yufor your kind recommendation of me to ye 
acquaintance of good Mr. Böhme, and when my affairs will 
permitt me more leisure, I hope to find more frequent opportunies
to profit myself of his conversation. He tells me that you 
desired me to assist him in inquiring concerning one Mr. Duval 
deceased, who had left some Legacy to your pious Foundation; I 
cannot yet gain any intelligence of such a person and wish you 
could give me some more particular information that might direct 
me to a more successfull search, for I shall be glad of all 
occasions to contribute my best services to yourself in 
partiular, and towards ye good work you are engag'd in. I have 
lately met with a Treatise touching ye pious Institution of 
Youth, wth which I have been much pleas'd, and as I thought it 
might also be acceptable to you, I have sent it to our good 
Friend Colonel Oyenhausen, praying him to forward ye same to you 
herewith. I pray God to prosper you lengthen your days, preserve
your health, & strengthen your hands for ye carrying on all your 
pious undertakings, and to bless your Labours therein; and I 
humbly committ you with my own soul to ye divine conduct of his 
Grace, desiring you also to give my affectionate salutes to my 
worthy friend Mr. Lang, and that you will both esteem of me as
Yr most faithfull Friend & humble Servant,
S Clement

Notes: Hague, Aprill 12th 1699
Sr.
Yours of ye 26th of March from Erfurt came to my hands late last 
night so our Letters being gone I could not then send forward 
that for Mr. Turner, which I will take care to do the very next 
post day. That to Ambassadour Lente I send this morning. Yours 
mentions that you sent word of the Chinese History of which I had
no notice but by the formention'd I am heartily glad of the book 
and hope the Providence of God will conduct it safe to me with 
some other wch I have encquired after from Mr. Franck. Whom I 
greatly Honour and Esteem, having besides other knowledge of him 
rec'd that which greatly recommends his Faith working by Love, I 
mean the account of his school which you order'd to be sent me 
from Amsterdam. It is my grief that I can make of use of it here
I live with a wretched Man that I doubt has neither Faith nor 
Charity I am sure tis to no purpose to communicate the History to
him; but I know it will be very pleasing to some good Christians 
of my acquaintance in England, and I hope to make some good use 
of it there; But alas I know not when I shall return thither 

Sr. Joseph has hired the House where my Lord Villers liv'd and we
are just upon remove thither, and he reckons upon staying six 
months longer. I am weary of a wicked disorderly Family, and I 
hope the Arch Bishop my Friend will call me over when an 
opportunity offers but that is an uncertainty; However, I desire 
when you think fit to write to me that you be pleased to direct 
your letter to be left for me with Mr. Philip Macdonald a B? 
Engelsche Domini at the Hague. I heartily pray that Heaven may 
accompany you with particular favor in all your travells, and 
blesse your pious endeavours wtih great success. I shall always
be very glad to hear from you where ever you are. I will now 
give you an account of part of a letter from the Arch Bishops 
Chaplain to whom I wrote condemning the Muscovite Priest. He 
answers it as follows:

"Immediately after the Czar was done, I went by my Lords order
to enquire after his Priest, with design to have shown him all 
the Civility possible but it weems it was thought fit to leave 
him with their numerous family at Amsterdam and it happned that 
the other Priest who came before with those who came to prepare 
lodgings here, fell sick and dyed, so that we were disappointed 
in all our good designs upon them. Some time since the Bishops 
with the Kings approbation thought fit to depute one of their 
Bench to wait upon the Czar in the name of the rest which was the
Bishop of Salisbury, whom the Czar recei'd very kindly, and among
other things signified his desire to see an Ordination of 
Ministers perform'd according to our Church. And (on such a 
Sunday) he with 3 or 4 more of his Company did us the HOnour to 
come hither for that end (that is to the Arch Bishops Pallace at 
Lambeth) this being thought the most private place where seeing 
no body but the Persons who officiated he was very much pleas'd. 
The persons Ordained were two, a Deacon and a Priest. The Bishop
of Norwich Ordai'd the Bishop of Salisbury read the LItany, and 
the Arch Bishop of Canterbury celebrated the Communion. The Czar
stood by the rails of the Communion table all teh while and was 
very observant of every thing, his Interpreter explaining 
particulars as they past. After this he went into the 
withdrawing Room where my Lord (that is the ArchBishop) made a 
short speech to him. A Banquet was prepar'd for him, but he only
eat a peice of bread, and drank 3 or 4 glasses of sack which is 
the wine he likes best. After he had seen the Library and staid 
here about 2 hours he went away expressig a great satisfaction in
all he had seen, and the next day sent his Physician to make his 
complement. It is said he designs for Vienna and Italy" 

I was not of his intending for our ? but have put our people in 
mind if they have opportunity to let him know of the 
Encouragement there for Greek scholars the King of Spans death is
much feared witch will make alterations in the World. But our 
Comfort is the Wise Providence of God? and governs all things. 
It is and will be a matter of grief and ? of our patience that we
cannot do the world so much good as we would but we may support 
our selves with this, that all things shall work together for 
good to them that Love God. May the Grace of our Lord Jesus 
Christ, the Love of God and the fellowship of the Holy Ghost be 
with you always. I remain
Sr. Your mmmost affectionate and humble servant
Theophilus Dorrington
Language: English

Hague
Siler
Düsseldorf
Notes: Reverend Sr.
I think fit to take this opportunity of writeing to you by the 
bearer hereof, tho by reason that he goes from Amsterdam on 
Saturday next I have not time to look into those things you have 
sent me before I write. I am in hast to returne you my hearty 
thanks for your great kindness in sending them. I am very glad 
to see so long and particular an account of the transaction of 
the Bishop of Niderstadt: and in order to understand it I have 
desired the Assistance of Domini Spitzey who has undertaken to 
get it translated into low Dutch for me. When I went to this 
Gentleman I found him such that I was glad I was entered into the
acquaintance of so worthy and sincere a man as he seems to be. 
And I the more willingly left the Manuscript with him because of 
the knowledge and esteem which he testified he has of you. I 
will take the utmost care that you may have it safe again. I am 
lamenting that I should give you and Mr. Ludolf so much trouble 
about Bidavai Historia Sinnia, and yet ? of it at last. It is 
indeed a book I have very greatly desir'd, but the person who 
promised you to bring it me has forgotten his promise, or his 
direction, for as yet I have heard nothing of it. I desire, if 
it may not be too much trouble, that you would send meword who he
was and where he dwells in Holland that I may demand it of him 
or direct him again where to send it for me. I expect that the 
Ambassadour with whom I am will be going from hence within these 
Months and consequently I shall then goe for England to, where 
Ishall endeavour to make our correspondence more serviceable to 
you and our fellow Christians of the Lutherane Church if it be 
possible, God grant it may redound to his Glory: I shall the 
mean while consider how to find out a fit person in Holland to be
the means of continueing a correspondence which I so much value 
at least for the sake of my own information and edification. I 
got leave a while agoe to make a little Journey into the adjacent
countries, and got up as far from hence as Coln; and comeing down
the Rhine to return home I met at Dusseldorp with a very worthy 
person, and one whom I value themore because he knows and exteems
you, I mean Domini Siler the Pasteur of the Lutherane Church 
there; I spent the morning of the Lords day in his Congregation, 
with a great deal of satisfaction beholding the order, teh 
solemnity, and devotion with which all the parts of the divine 
worship were perform'd. He seems to be a very good Man and, if it
may be, I prupose to correspond with him. Let us remember one 
another at the Altar, the throne of Grace, and pray for the Peace
of Jerusalem. I conclude for the present with assurances that I 
am, Reverend Sr.,
your most Affectionate and Humble servant
Theophilus Dorrington

Hague July 10th n.st.1699.

Reference Type:  Generic
Record Number: 329
Author: Ebenezer, Saltzburgers at
Year: 1739
Secondary Author: Europe, benefactors in
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1739/10/26
Type of Work: printed letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/35:13 [10302]
England Fasc. II, s. 61/162; Halle: 30, 2; Film nr. 20, 1058

Custom 1: 1739-10-26
Keywords: Ebenezer
Georgia
Boltzius John Martin
Grownau Israel Christian
SPCK
England
Notes: The SOCIETY for Promoting Christian
Knowledge having, under the Providence of GOD, been greatly 
instrumental in raising such charitable and liberal 
Contributions, as have enabled them to settle the Protestant 
Emigrants from Saltzburg at Ebenezer in the English Colony of 
Georgia, think themselves obliged to make the following Letters 
publick, that the World may know how just and religious a Sense 
of Gratitude and Joy these honest and good People have, for all 
the Blessings and Favours they have received from God and their 
Benefactors in the Days of their Distress; and that those also 
among us who are blessed with tan Ability of doing more abundant 
Good, may be satisfied how well their Charity will be bestowed in
a further Supply of such spiritual and temporal Wants as are 
signify'd by them to the SOCIETY, till they have it in their own 
Power to render their Settlement compleat.

A Translation of a Letter out of High Dutch, from teh 
Saltzburgers at Ebenezer to their Benefactors in Europe.

We, whose Names are underwritten, the Saltzburgers and all the 
Members of the Communion of Ebenezer in Georgia in America, 
present our most humble and most dutiful Respects, and good 
Wishes to all our kind Benefactors and Benefactresses in England 
and Germany, of all Ranks and Conditions whatsoever.

To the Praise of Almighty GOD we often call to remembrance all 
the spiritual and temporal Kindnesses and Favours which we have 
received from manyThousands of true Protestant Countries; and 
therefore we think it our bounden Duty, as long as we live, 
humbly to implore our gracious LORD, in the Name of JESUS CHRIST,
through the Assistance of theHOLY GHOST, who has inclined their 
Hearts to Charity and good Will towards us, that He would be 
plesed according to his great Mercy to reward all their Works of 
Love wih abundant Blessings intheLife thatnow is, and in that 
which is to come.

The wonderful and all-wise Providence having open'd a Way for us 
to go to Georgia, a new Colony, begun in good measure for the 
Refuge and Support of persecuted and distressed Protestants; and 
we, after a previous due Consideration of the Will of GOD, having
gone thither with a full Inclination and Chearfulness of Mind: 
The Love and Benevolence of our ever honoured Benefactors towards
us despised People has not been altered in the least, but we have
had the comfortable Experience of it in many Instances, as well 
at our Departure from Europe as also ever since at Ebenezer; the 
Place, where, by GOD's Assistance and Blessing, we have taken up 
our Abode. Before we left Germany we were provided with 
necessary Protestant Books, and such as we still wanted have been
sent after us in such plenty, that we cannot sufficiently praise 
the LORD for those Blessings. Upon our Arrival in this Country, 
wherein wewere quite Strangers, we found the want of Linnen and 
other Necessaries for the cloathing of our Bodies; but GOD 
almighty has beyond our Expectation so graciously order'd it, 
that from Year to Year, bythe kind Contributions of several 
Benefactors, a good Stock thereof has been sent to us, which has 
filled our Hearts with Praise and thanksgiving; And tho' an 
uncultivated Country, in a new Climate, together with a Way of 
Living quite different from what we were accustomed to before, 
couldnot but occasion various Diseases and Distempers, as did 
likewise the want of Shoes and other Necessaries among our Poor; 
yet the merciful GOD has inclined the Hearts of our worthy 
Benefactors, to make Remittances from time to time for these 
Purposes into the Hands of our Ministers, and more particularly 
we have been sufficiently provided with excellent Medicines, 
which have often had their desired Effect. Besides the liberal 
Charities in Money given to the Third Transport, as also to some 
of the Second, who came from Lindau to Ebenezer, and since that, 
to the seven new Colonists; the All-sufficient GOD has likewise 
continually blessed us with such Supplies, that we have been able
both to erect and support an Orphan-House or Hospital among us; 
which has been very much to the spiritual and temporal Advantage 
of the whole Congregation; and will continue to be so, if, as we 
wish and pray, te Fountain of GOD's Mercy shall still flow upon 
us. We cannot also but esteem it to be a very acceptable 
Benefit, and worthy of our most sincre Thanks, that so many good 
and pious Persons in Europe go on to promote our Welfare with 
their earnest Prayers, Intercessions, good Wishes, Counsels and 
Christian Exhortations; but above all we acknowledge, with the 
deepest Sense of Gratitude, that the LORD, according to his 
loving Kindness, has lrgely provided us with his holy Word and 
Sacrament, togehter with all things necessary for this Life, 
particularly with a plentiful Harvest last Year; as also that He 
has disposed the Honourable the Trustees of Georgia, and the 
SOCIETY for Promoting Christian Knowledge, together with other 
Benefactors in England, to favour and assist us in a singular and
extraordinary Maner; for which the Name of the Giver of every 
good and perfect Gift be fo ever praised ny us and all our 
Posterity.

In order, therefore, to shew our most worthy Benefactors the real
Sense we have of the charitable Gifts and Kindnesses we have 
receiv'd from them we think ourselves bound both in Duty and 
Gratitude to write this Letter in order to be published, wishing 
from the bottom of our Hearts, that the GOD of eternal Truth, the
Almighty CREATOR of Heaven and Earth, (who is pleased with 
Sacrifices of Mercy) may abundantly reward all their Charities 
betowed upon us, and so bless this their Seed that they may reap 
a plentiful Harvest of eternal Joy and Happiness in the Life to 
come, for our LORD and Saviour will not forget his gracious 
Promise: Matt. xxv. 34. 36. "Then shall theKin say unto them 
on his right hand, Come, ye blessed of my Father, inherit the 
Kingdom prepared foryou from the Foundation of the World: for I 
was an hungry, and ye gave me Meat; I was thirsty, and ye gave me
drink; I was a Stranger, and ye took me in; naked, and ye 
cloathed me, etc." but will fulfil it to the eternal 
Satisfaction and Comfort of all such as are not weary in well 
doing: As long as we shall live we shall not cease, by the 
Assistance of the Holy Spirit, humbly to implore, in our publick 
and private Prayers, our heavenly Father, that he would encompass
them with his Favour as with a Shield; and make good to them and 
their Children all his precious Promises, more especially that in
Psalm xli. I.3 Blessid is he that considereth the Poor, the Lord 
will deliver him in the time of Trouble: the Lord will preserve 
him and keep him alive, and he shall be blessed upon the Earth; 
and thou wilt not deliver him unto the Will of his Enemies. the 
Lord will strengthen him upon the Bed of Languishing; thou wilt 
make all his Bed in his Sickness." And as we do further 
humbly conceive, that it will not be unacceptable to such our 
Friends and Benefactors to be acquainted ih our present 
Circumstances in this new Part of the World; we beg leave to 
inform them, to the Praise of theliving GOD, who has done all 
Things well, that we at Ebenezer live in the happy and 
fcomfortable Enjoyment of a pure, and plentiful Instruction in 
the holy Gospel; of many temporal Blessings; of all Christian 
Liberty; of external Tranquility, and good Success in our 
Undertakings, and also in brotherly Love and Charity to one 
another: the Sense of which Mercies, even whilst it convinces us
of our great Unworthiness, does at the same time make us wish, 
out of Love to our Brethren and Countrymen in Germany, that they 
also might be Partakers wiih us of these Blessings.

Our new erected Town, Ebenezer, is situated so very conveniently 
on the River Savannah, as to be far enough removed from the noise
of the World and worldly minde Men. the Land granted for our 
Plantations is very good, and has even this Year given us a full 
Proof of its Fertility, and what it is able, by the Blessing of 
GOD to produce. Our Cattle increases; the keeping of Herdsmen to
look after them is made easy to us, by their being for the most 
part maintained by Charity Money sent over from Europe to our 
Ministers. As to the blessed Effects of the Ministry of our 
loving Teachers, and what the most gracious GOD is pleased to do 
by them for our Souls, Eternity will make appear. The Eyes of 
many amongst us have been opened in this Wilderness, so that 
Ebenezer has been to several the Place of their spiritual Birth. 
Our Place of Divine Worship has been hitherto in a Hut, which in 
Winter and rainy Seasons is very inconvenient; nor have we any 
Place for the Education of our Children; but we trust GOD will 
also therein hear our Prayers, and by the charitable 
Contributions of well disposed Christians, enable us to build a 
Church and School-House. We have already signified these 
ourWants to some of our Friends in Europe; and may GOD Almighty 
so stir up the Hearts of some who abound in teh Blessings of this
Life, that they may give out of their Abundance, what will be 
sufficient towards raising so necessary and useful Edifices.

We conclude this our Letter with commending you, our ever 
renouwned Benefactors, to the everlasting Love of God the Father,
to the tender Grace of our Lord JESUS CHRIST, and to the 
comfortable Fellowship of the HOLY GHOST, now and for evermore; 
and at the same time assuring you of our constant and earnest 
Prayers for your true Happiness and Welfare, we remain, with 
profoundest Respects,
Your mot humble (and for so many spiritual and temporal Benefits,
in Love and Gratitude) most obliged Servants, 
The Inhabitants of Ebenezer,
Ebenezer in Georgia, 
26th Octob. 1739

A Translation of a letter out of High Dutch, from the Ministers 
of the Saltzburgers at Ebenezer.

Dear and Hnoured Benefactors and Friends in Christ our Lord,

We think it our Duty to accompany this Letter of our Congregatio 
with a few Lines, as being, by your Will adn Pleasure, intitled 
to a Share in the many Favours you have bestowed upon them, and, 
consequently, being obliged to united with them in Praises and 
Thanksgivings to GOD for his Mercies, as well as in humble 
Intercessions for your Welfare and Happiness.

We can assuredly testify of our Saltzburgers, that they have 
received all the Benefactions sent and distrubtued to them, wiht 
the greatest Humility and Thankfulness, express'd in the most 
obliging and respectful Terms; and have made use fo them 
agreeably to the Intent of the Givers, to the Glory of GOD, and 
the Relief of their own Necessities. As often as they join with 
us in Prayer (as we do not only every Day at Evening Prayer, but 
several times a Week besides, either in our own Houses or theirs 
when we go to visit them) the Benefactions received are always 
mentioned with Praise toGOD, and Wishes for his Blessing on all 
their Benefactors. They beg of GOD Almighty to give them Grace 
to apply all such Benefactions to the Ends they are sent for, and
that they may be led by this his Goodness towards them to 
Repentance and Holiness of Life. Altho' it is too common for 
many to spend what is bestowed on them even in Charity in an 
irregular and sinfulManner, yet we cannot say this of any one o 
our Saltzburgers; nay we should ourselves evven on any Suspicion 
of this kind, have rather kept back the Benefactions designed for
such Persons till their Amendment should appear, than to allow a 
worng Use of them; in doing which we hope that we act nothing 
contrary to the Will and Intention of our Benefactors. We can 
therefore assure all our Patrons and Friends upon our best 
Knowledge and Conscience, and we hope to their great 
Satisfaction, that they have not sown the Seed of their Charities
upon a barren, but in a fertile Growund at Ebenezer, where it 
will blossom and bring forth Fruits unto everlasting Life: And 
since according to the Testimony of the Holy Spirit, this is the 
Portion of the Righteous, that it shall be well with them, and 
that they shall eat the Fruit of their Doings; we never shall 
cease to make our hearty Supplications before our most faithful 
and merciful Father inHeaven, that He may fulfil on them this and
all his other precious Promises; that in return for what they 
have given so liberally to the poor Saltzburgers, or rather lent 
unto the LORD, they may receive a thousand fold, through the 
Merit and Mediation of JESUS CHRIST.
Part of the Charities in Money and other Gifts has been, 
according to the Pleasure of the Benefactors, a great help to 
both of us Ministers, in the first settling our Families; for 
which we humbly praise the LORD, and return them our most 
grateful Acknowledgments. The LORD grant unto them, that they 
may find Mercy of the LORD inthat Day; and as they have refreshed
us so often, they may togeher with their worthy Families be 
refreshed in the Presence of theLORD for ever, yea that Goodness 
and Mercy may follow them all the Days of their Life. THese, 
dearest Benefactors, are the hearty Wishes and daily Prayers of 
Your very obliged humble Servants,
John Martin Boltzius, Minister of theSaltzburgers at Ebenezer
Israel Christian Gronau, Catechist and Assistant to the 
Congregation of Saltzburgers at Ebenezer.

Ebenezer in Georgia, 26th Octb. 1739
Language: English

Notes: London 
den 12 Junii 1726
Aus der übeflüßigen Fütte Jesu wünsche Gnade 
um Gnade!

Hocwürdiger und Hochgelehrter, insoders Hochgeehrtester Herr
Großer Gönner!

ich kan die güte Gottes nicht enugsam preisen, daß sie 
mir nicht nur eine glückliche und behaltene, sondern auch 
kurtze und dazu angenehme plesier? reise aus lauter gnade 
geschencket. dem wir haben nur 9 tage auf der Elbe, See und 
Thames nacher London ja biß in die Stadt hinein zu gebracht. 
Und kan versichern, daß das waßer Thames aus mit hohern 
Wellen empfangen, und in dem hoffen eingeführet hat, als das 
großewelt were? wo durch wir gekommen sind, gethan hat. die 
ursach ist veil wir nicht nur auf der Elbe, sondern auch auf der 
See beständig mittelmäßigen favorabeln Wind gehabt, 
und auf dem Revir nacher London ist der Wind contrair und 
ungestürm gewesen. doch aber nachdem wir ein Tag und nacht 
auf der Elbe, 5 tage auf der Seeund 3 tage und drey nächte 
auf der Thames gefahren, sind wir mit allem Seelen, die auf den 
Schif gewesen, gesund und wohl gottlob angelanget Ew 
hochwürden zu berichten, was sich im Hamburg zugetragen, wie 
ich daselbst empfangen un tractiret worden, erachte 
überfüßig zu seyn, Weil der herr Teckeenburg es schon
längst auf mein bitte wird berichtet haben. Mir lieget also 
ob meiner pflicht=Schuldigkeit gemäß, der gantzen 
hochlöblichen Theologischen Facultaet und ins besondern Ew. 
Hochwürden mit wenigen, weil ich aus mangel das raums noch 
kurtz faßen muß, vor alle genozsene güte, 
Väterliche liebe, versorgung und recommendation mein 
Schuldige dancksagung ab zu statten und mein erkentliches 
gemüth hiemit nochmahls zu contestiren, Wie auch mit diesem 
Wenigen seilen zu eröffnen, wie viel daro wohlgemeinte 
recommendation an den Herrn Pastor Ziegenhage ausgewircket. So 
bald der gütige GOtt mich aus land geholffen habe ich mich 
also bald nacher St. James wo der Herr Pastor Ziegenhagen wohnet,
verfüget, und ihm daro angenehmens Schreiben überrichet, 
und ob er Wohl vor sich bezeügte, daß er mir nach allem 
vermögen gerne behülflich seyn wolte, so muße 
vernehmen, daß gegenwärtig allem ansehen noch vor micch 
allhier kein unterkommen seyn würde. Nach verfließung 
etlicher Tage ging ich abermahl zu den Herrn Pastor Ziegenhagen, 
und befragte ihm, of er es vor gut befinde, daß ich mich bey 
den Bischp von London melden, und meine dienste nacher West 
Indien antragen solte, und da er darinnen consentirte, machte 
also fort mein aufwendung bey demselben, offerirte meine 
wenigkeit zum dienst der Kirche in West Indien, u. erhielt 
daß versprochen, daß er mich dahin senden wolte, wenn ich
gute Zeügniße meins lebens und Wandels hier in England 
und auf Universitaeten aufweisen Konte. Bies ichnun hievon den 
Herr Pastor Ziegenhagen rapport gethan, und um ein Testimonium 
meines Wohlverhaltnus auf Universitaeten ans dero recommendations
Schreiben anhielten, war er also fort willing mir daßelbe auf
beste, als nur immer könnte, mit Zutheilen. Ich erhielte auch
von dem Eltesten einferner gemeine davon der Selige Vater 
gestanden, ein schönes Zeügniß Mit diesem Testimoniis
versehen, nahm ich gleich gelegenheit die selben dan Bishop zu 
ügerlieffern, und nach dem sie von dem Herrn Dr. Gerdesio, 
dar auf das Herr pastor Ziegenhagens und meine ansuchen mit mir 
zum Bischopginge, al wahre und ächte Zeügniße sind 
verificiret worden, bin ich examinirt und dem Contag Trinitatis 
in der Pauli Kirche öffentlich ordiniret worden. Und hie von
hätte ich sollen? Posttage ehr nachricht ertheilen, (crossed 
out section) ? auch zu gleich willens gewesen zuberichten in 
welchen theil und Ort in West Indien ich geschickt worden soll, 
habe ichs biß her austehen laßen. da aber der Secretair 
des Bischop gleich noch der Ordination wiedermuthen ist ins land 
verreist und noch nicht wieder kommen, und es zu lange dauern 
möchte, als habe ich nicht länger mein Schreibens 
aufhalten können. Was meine geringe person? betrift, so 
haben den vater aller barmhertzigkeit höchlich zu preisen 
für diesen Success und bißher verlichner gesundheit, und 
daß er mich die füßstaffen seiner güte in meinen 
kümmerlichen umständen sehen undfinden läßet. das
wenige geld, daß ich in London mitgebracht ist theils auf der
reise, theils hier vor Zehrung, theils for kleidung aufgegangen. 
Meine Frau und kind sind gott lob gesund, aber ich habe sie 
biß dito aus mangel des geldes ? besuchen können, dan sie
sind 16 teusche meile von London. Einen brieff habe empfangen und
ersehe darause daß sie willens ist England zu verlaßen. 
Dürfte also ohne ehr nacher Wet Indien gehen müßen. 
der H. Past. Ziegenhagen ist so gütig gewesen und hat mir 10 
shchillings 6 pence ? vergeschoßen ich muß hier 
schließen und Ew. Hochwürden der göttlichen obhüt
empfehlen undmit anweisching länges leben.....{too tiny to 
read! closes letter}
gehorsamster diener Esdras Theodorus Edzardi

PS:
Wenn ich von hier reisen, wurde außer wan Zweiffel etwas geld
von den bischopbekommen und als den können Ew. 
hochwürdig. versichert seyn, daß ich meine abreise und 
was sonst sich zutragen möchte, unfehlbar melden wurde. 
bitte auch gehoramst der sämtliche hochlöblichen 
Theologischen Facultaet meinen Schuldigsen respect und 
gebuhrenden veneration anzuzeigen. Wie auch meinen freund 
Schüldigsten grüß an den Herrn pastor Freylingshausen
unbeschwert zu vermeldten.

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 20
Author: Falckner, Daniel
Year: 1691
Title: Lübeck
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1691/08/26
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 32/11:3 [10902]
Amerika Fasc. XII, S. 1108/9; Halle: 32, 11; Film nr. 22, 831
Custom 1: 1691-08-26
Custom 2: 53.865467, 10.686559
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Keywords: Falckner Daniel
Falckner
Lübeck
Breithaupt
Denner Jacob
Noldo
Francke
Abstract: Falckner bringt seine Verbundenheit mit Francke und [J. J.] Breithaupt zum Ausdruck.
Notes: Das Bewendige Wortt Leite aus aus der Kraft
zur Kraft Zur halten einen Sieg nach dem andern und Führe uns
nach seinen guten belieben ein in die selbige Gemeinschaft seiner
Beyden Zur ähnlichkeit seines Todtes Ja Amen!

Gesegneter und Gesalbter des Herrn.

Eben da ich diesen Wunsch aus überflus meines Hertzens 
ausgeschriebein, umb noch wenige Zeilen diesen bey zu fügen, 
Sehe, so Kombt der Liebe Semler und benachrichtiget mich von dem 
Erfurtlichen Zustande. Nun kan ich wohl sagen, daß meine in 
die 3 Tage süftzende Seele in eine hohe freüde über 
darumbstandlichen gezehlung gezogen wurde, so das ich mich nicht 
begreiffen künte, der Herr der allwisende Weis, was das 
Geistes Sein ist, Er es gelebet in Ewigkeit und alles Volck sage 
Amen!

Aber du mein Jesu, ist es dem die Zeit, das sich deine 
getreüre Zeügen bis an die Bande und des Evangelii willen
leiden sollen, ich find keine andere antwortt also ja im meiner 
Seele, und sehe im Geiste gleichsam die Freudigkeit Petri und 
Johannis in ihren angesichtern. Ja ihr Väter die ihr eines? 
gezeüget durch das Wortt der warheit ihr habt uns dieses 
Prognosticon von anfang, da ihr uns als kindern die 
Göttlichen warheiten orgetragen, gestellet, wollen so gehet 
denn ein her in Kraft des Herrn Herrn, zu eurer Zeit, die Gottes 
Zeit ist, wird auch eüer Nahme verworfen als ein 
Schändlicher, der Herr wird mich und alle gegen welche ihr 
Mutterlich gewesn seyd, treü machen, das wen Er will, wir mit
euch die Schmach Christi ausen vor dem Thore tragen. Vustet 
getrost der Herr der allgewältige hat es euch geheisen. 
Fürchtet euch nicht, dann derer sind mehr die bey Euch sind, 
dann bey ihnen. Hüpfet und jubiliret denn der Konig der 
Ehren, welche ihr vorhindiget hab, sich auf gemacht in verborgen 
doch mit gewaltigen arm Euch zu führen. Von nun an soll der 
Geist der Herrlichkeit zurfältige auf euch ruhen, da ihr umb 
Christo willen sollet zum Fryopfer werden. Warte ich auf 
gedencke mit wollenden hertzen daran, daß der Herr viel 
gefäse der Chron sich zu bereitet habe, die seine Chron mit 
ihren blüte zu versiegeln fertig sein werden. So werde dann 
das Evangelium geprediget in der gantzen Welt zu einem 
Zeügnis uber sie Hallelujah sey dem warhaftigen Gott, der 
nach dem die Zeit der Verwirrung über Isräel kommen ist, 
er mitten in der Finsternus sein Lucht? so helle herrn 
Leüchten lasen und auch uns von der Finsternus zu seinen 
wunderbahren lüchte berufen und das geistes Erstlinge 
gegeben. Er erbarme sich doch umb seines Sohnes unsers 
Erlösers willen meiner und aller andern, die mit mir eben 
denselben theüren glauben am seiner Sohn bekammen haben, das 
wir Reich werden in der Lobe, damit der Glaubige Leib unsers 
Heilandes, durch dieses band der Vollen Kommenheit gezieret und 
Verbunden werde, das wir nach einer Vogelein hergehen und die 
Ewigkeit im Geiste fast halten lernen. das ist mein Wundsch und 
Flehen, welches immer zu dem Herren gerichtet ist. 

Den Theüren Knecht Gottes H. D. Breithaupt bitte hertzlich zu
Grüßen. Der Herr Kröhne ihm mit vielen Seegen und 
Schenke ihm ein gerütteltes Maas des Geistes; Er lasse ihm 
ferner Brüllen, wie einen Löwen, den man seine jungen 
rauben will; hingegen auch gedultig leiden, wie ein Lamm. Er vor
binde ihre Seelen in tiefter Einigkeit des Geistes, das sie nicht
ermünden in den Kampft mit denen wilden Thieren zu Epheso. 
Nun der Herr ist ihre Stärcke und Fels, ihr segneten, darumb 
stehet euer Haus feste was wollen ihre Stur winde thun, die Stadt
Gottes soll demnach sein lustig bleiben.

Sonsten habe mit gegebener Briefe nebst der commission an H. D. 
Noldo bestellet, und war gut das ich das befohlen in meiner 
Schreib Tafel stehen hatte, sonst wäre er nicht mit mir zu 
Frieden gewesen. Er hat mich aus geforschet und mich 
genöthiget, das ich es ihm aus meiner Schreibe Tafel auf 
papier schreiben müsen. ich habe sollen zu ihm zu Tische 
kommen, aber weil es nur auf schertz und aus forschung angesehen 
war, habe ich es gewisens halber nicht thun können. 

Sonsten habe ich mich den Herrn überlasen, wegen Jacob Denner
saget er denn auch selbst die wege also aufgeschlosen, daß 
ich unmöglich habe entrennen können nochwollen. Ich 
halte mich stille und einsam, solange, alß Gott will mit 
großer Freyheit im Gewissen; verspühre auch die Gnade des
Herrn zur information; 

sonsten habe 3 Tage grose angst gehabt, da ich aus seinen hause 
in einen der haus zihen wollen, welche angst erst bey scheidung 
dieses briefs ein wenig verschwunden. Ich habe ja ohn 
unterlaß mit vielen seuftzen? vor dem Herrn mich ein reines 
und in allen gehorsahmes hertzens so las mich euch derselbe, dem 
ich bitte, nicht zweifels, das er mich nur nach seinen willen 
führen werde.

Der lobe Jacob denner grüset inniglich und ist ihrer mit 
Thränen sonsten vor dem Herrn vielmahl eingedenck Nun der 
Her sey sein licht und hoch und seines lebens kraft von nun an 
bis in Ewigkeit. Ich verbleibe, meines innigst gelobten Bruders 
aufrichtiger bruder, Daniel Falckner

Lübeck d. 26. Augusti ao 1691

die liebe Brüder und Schwestern bitte herzlich zu grüsen,
ich hätte an dem lieben H. D. Breithaupt selber geschrieben 
wann die zeit es zu gelasen, kann das mein hertz in eil in diese 
noten aus fliesen konnen. Mein bruder der noch etzliche Tage bei
mir verbleibet grüset sie

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 26
Author: Falckner, Daniel
Year: 1692
Title: Lüneburg
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1692/02/08
Type of Work: Letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 32/11:4 [10903]
Amerika Fasc. XII, s. 1110/1; Halle: 32, 11; Film nr. 22, 833
Custom 1: 1692-02-08
Custom 2: 53.249950, 10.408870
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Keywords: Spener
Semler
Falckner Daniel
Denner Jacob
Lauterbach
Franckfurt
Pfeiffer
Weidling
Hamburg
Lübeck
Halberstadt
Nürnberg
Berlin
Notes: Lüneburg, d. 8. Febr. 1692

Mein Geseegneter des Herrn,
Seine Hertzlichen und sorgfältige Lieber hat mir ein 
offenbahres Zeügnüß nach dem willen unßers Vaters
gäen müßen durch das Schreiben, Welches von 21 Jan. 
an mich datiret von Hern Semlern mir nach Lüneburg geschickt 
worden. 

Die zu versicht in seiner Seelen von meiner treue im glauben und 
in der Liebe Versigelt meine Hoffnung in dem Geiste Jesu Christi,
daß, ob mich schon meine untreu scham roth machet vor des 
Hern angesichten dennoch der Zerstöhrer der Höllen 
Tilger? des unglaubens und Zweiffels durch die reine Fülle 
seiner un veränderlichen liebe dem grund eines 
allerheiligsten und Lautoren in reiner Liebe Thätigen 
Glaubens ferner legen meine Mängel, die Zwar noch groß 
umb seiner Ewigen Erbarmung zu denken und durch den Kraft seiner 
leiden und auferstehung zur vollständigen gebuhrt der 
neüen Creatur in der ihm wohlgefälltigen Maße mir 
selbst Verhelffen werde. Den Er alleine ist es, in Welcher meine
Seele Suche Heyl und Selligkeit Findet, Und nach dem ich ihm dem 
Süßen Heilend zu seinen ewigen Preiß alß dem 
Mittler Zweiffen mir den ungerechten und vordanckten und dem ewig
gerechten Gott in meiner Seele mit seinen Mittler ampt wahr 
genommen, und noch täglichen warhnehme wie sein 
allerheiligstes blut vergießen das unheilige Ergießen 
meines Fleisches zur beflehung des Geistes zu ruckehält und 
sein friede mich bewahret u. mich Elenden und geringsten! 
Daß ich nicht thue dem willen der Vernunft und der Höhen,
die sich erheben wider die Erkändtnüß Jesu, so sehnet
sich meine Seele, ja sie sehnet sich, und wird fast vor der 
innigsten geistes begierde Kranck in seiner Kraft ohne Verzug und
hinderung doch stiller und leidender weise zu laufen nach dem 
Kleinodt?, damit Er auch mein alles in allen werden mögen. 
In ansehung dieses werde Ich gehalten nicht nur zu vergeßen, 
was dafinden ist, sondern meiner Seele beginnet zu Ekeln vor 
aller Stückwerck und Erkändtnüß und findet ruhe 
mit stillen und unverrichten Geist auf dem Hern wie die augen der
Knechte und Magde zu sehen, Weil ja Christum lieb haben beßer
ist dann alle wißen und dieses ist so viel ich da von 
begreiffen und schreiben kan mein innerlicher zustand, darinnen 
mich der Herr biß auffgegen wartige Stunde erhält mit 
hertzlicher innigster begierde in seiner Liebe gewurzelt zu 
werden.

Mein außwendiger zustand welcher zu wißen verlunt wird, 
kan von mir selbst nicht wohl beschreiben worden, dann weil ich 
bey mir selbst zu hauser bin und von dem Hern mit stillen und 
freüdigen Gesite biß itz gehalten werde, so nehme ich 
das, was außer mir ist nicht wahr; 

Von dem lieben Denner bin ich nicht ohne gewißheit weg 
gezogen, der Herr sey gelobet der mich vor absichten bewerhret, 
wo hin mich nun der Herr Führen werden, weiß ich noch 
nicht, nur daß sein willen geschehen darzu ich mich dan auch 
seiner Liebe und andacht befohle.

Ich bin beruffen nach Nürnberg, nach Berlin und Halberstadt, 
der Herr wird ja dem der gerne Einfältig werden will 
behüten und ihm dem besten Weg zeigen

Ich reise nun von hier wider nach Hamburg, mag sein daß ich 
mich allda noch 1 oder 2 wochen aufhalten. Mein Seele und geist 
freuen sich über den herrlichen und sehligen Führungen 
die der Her mit Ihm seinen gefüße der Ehre vornimmbt und 
sie wohl hinauß führet. Wie führet doch der Hohe und
Erhabene die Elenden so Herrlich und wie mächtig ist seine 
rechte mit denen warhaftigen die doch alß verführer 
geachtet werde darüber hört man froloken im Tempel des 
Herrn und jaüchsen in seinen Heiligthum, wen jubiliren die 
Herrschaft der Himmelen da die Sünder zur Buße geruffen 
kommen zum abendmahl des lammes Hallelujah sey Jesu Christo dem 
Ewigen Konigen, der seine brunlein auf die gaßen fließen 
läßet daß ? trincken und gesund worden und die freye 
und offene Thur zu der Ewigen Erlösungen mit gewißen 
tritten betreten. Hallelujah Sey dem Vater, der uns auf diese 
Zeiten auf behalten, da sey ewiger wille in ausbreitung und 
Eröffnung seiner unergrundlichen Liebe gleichsam aufneue an 
die gewißen der Menshe offenbahret und die sich dieser 
Seeligkeit selbst wertsachen in der gnade zu glauben und zu 
leiden umb des Nahmens Jesu von Nazareth verseegelt werden. 
Hallelujah, Sey denn Geist der warheit der unter so vielen 
zweiffeln die Ja kommen und erst kommen werden, uns so 
treülich in die Warheit leitet und die weißheit umb den 
Thron Gottes mittheilet, welche alle geister durch dringen lernet
wie scharf und behend sie sind; Ja dieser einige und ewige Gott, 
daß selligfreund aller vollen kommenster licht, sey gelobet 
von alle dem was adam hat und was Ihm dienet, Hallelujah Amen, 

Mein Hertz bruter sich aus in der Liebe zu denselben, wie wohl es
die Zeit izo nicht wohl leidet Weitlauftig zu sorgen was wegen 
Ich die nahmen der Glaubigen in Lübeck zu berichten nur 
biß zu einer andern Zeit vor behalten muß.

Herr Weidling und seiner Frau habe geschrieben wohl 3 mahl habe 
aber nicht mehr alß eine antwort bekommen, die mir und nach 
denckens gemachet, wo ich meine Sinnlichkeit hinein begeben 
hatte. Er berichtete unter andern von seiner Frau, daß sie 
traurig und unglaubig wäre nebst der leidlichen Kranckehit. 

Ich bin auch erfreuet über der gelungenen widerkehr des M. 
Speners zu dem Herrn. Es grüßen demselben und andere 
lieben hertzen die geschmächeten und verfolgten allhie, an 
welchen wir die wirckung des Gesites der Herrligkeit zum lobe 
Gottes und Früdigkeit unser glaubens sehen. 

Es grüßet der hertliebe Pfeiffer welche itzo auch by uns.

Ingleich der Liebe Lauterbach welcher izo hier und so der Herr 
will beyseiner zuruck reise nach Franckfurth ihre angesichter 
sehen wird und sie seegnen unter der Ewigen Erbarung bin Ich und 
habe die hoffnung zu bleiben. Eines der gereisen glieder andem 
H. Liebe Jesu.
Daniel Falckner.

Author: Falckner, Daniel

Title: Hamburg

Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 32/11:5 [10904]
Amerika Fasc. XII, s. 1106/7; Halle: 32, 11; Film nr. 22, 835
Custom 1: 1693-01-27

Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Keywords: Falckner Daniel
Hamburg
Francke
Notes: Hamburg, d. 27 jan. 1693
? Lauter Gnade Gottes in Christo durchdringe uns mit ihrer 
Lauterkeit in der warheit durch die Kräftige Würkung des 
Reinen Geistes Amen Hallelujah!

Au serWelter des Herrn
Nach dem in Christo mir ein Geist seinen heiligen Leibregieret 
daß die Wharen glieder dasßelben also unter einander in 
dem lichte gemeinschaft finden, so bin auch ich daß geringste
überschwanglich in Freuden, nach dem ich theils höre 
theils mich in guter hoffnung Versichere, wie Er ünser 
gereuer Immanuel sich herrlich beweiset bey ihnen und also sein 
Nahmen, wie sein Ruhm in der Kraft mit gewißer Versiegeliung 
aler Gottes Verheißung in ihm nach seiner mannichfaltigen 
Weißheit und in beschränkten Wurkung offenbahr wird, O Er
wird noch di s und das darzu thun und seine Verheißungen Weit
überschwenglicher an uns läsen alß die Enge unserer 
Vernunfte ja unser Geist selbst wird erreichen können. 
Gewiß der Sieg ist an das Creuze jesu Christi angeheftet Wir 
wollen hinzu treten die thörischte Kraft Gottes wird unsere 
Närrin die Vernunft gefangen nehmen daß wie wir zum 
Zeugnuß der gebuhrt aus Gott daß leben aus Gott in unsern
Gesite finden also auch die nach folge Christi in solcher geburth
des Lebens bey uns immer gesegnter erfolge, damit unter solchem 
gehorsam des glaubens ein guter schatz aufs zu künftgie uns 
gesamlet bleibe und die gnade zu leiden in dem Geiste der 
Herligkeit unser ruhm, freüde, Ruhe, und erwünschter Sieg
seyn in gelaßener übergabe an die gewaltige hand unsers 
Vaters, So Lauffen wir ein mahls auffs ungewiße. Ein solch 
vertrauen haben wir durch Christum zu Gott dem getreuen und 
warhaftigen dem Lebendigen und allmächtigen, und wer wird 
seyn, der uns also spaden könne so wir dem guten nach kommen,
genug, wer in Gott ist, hat sich niemahls vor fleisch zu 
fürchten Tobt ihr voller; Lebb ihr kinder, Kriegt ihr 
wölfe, Siegt ihr lämmer, der Er stehet auf in seiner 
Kraft, Er erhebet sich in seiner Macht, daß Eer gedencke an 
seinen bund, ja, ja, der Sieg ist offenbahr denn auch seine 
gerichte werden offenbahr und die bothen des Himmels tragen sich 
mit der Zeitung das das kindgebohren und diese Zeit ihr Ziel 
erreichet, daß die andere Zeit auch herbey komme, die Hundert
Tausend so vor ihm stehen und die 1000000 so ihm dienen sind 
bereit in der bewegung aller kräften zu bemerken daß der 
Vernunft ihr urtheil her? kommen ? der Stab ist gebrochen in den 
himmeln Wer will und kan denn nun der Straffe deiner Blutschulden
aufhalten du wild viel kopffiches Thier? O Herr hilff uns, ja du
thut es dein Nahme und dem reichen enspalle mit ewigen Hallelujah
durch die Chörd der himlichen Sänger biß in den 
abgrund deiner unerforschlichen tieffen, daß es ewig 
wiederspalle und alles erfüllet seyn von gethäne deiner 
Weißheit und Warheit, deiner Macht und deiner Wunder ja Amen.
Hallelujah!
Mein bruder Er Freue sich mit denen Kindern, welche also schreyen
müßen da der König ein herzeücht der Warheit zu 
guth, daß Er den Vater, wie er ihm ver klähre und 
vollende sein Werck in und durch seinen heiligen liebe nach der 
mächtigen Würkung seines Geistes Zum ewigen Wundere 
Hallelujah! Seiner andacht vor dem Herrn wird mich elenden der 
selbe einige Gesit der im Geiste Zions Zeuget, ein Verleiben 
damit ich lauterlich allerwegen Thun möge ? 
Wohlgefälligen willen Gottes und unseres Christi, darzu ich 
demselben auch mit innigkeit der unergrundlichen und wesentlichen
Liebes Erbarmung empfehlend Verbleiben des l. br. mittgenoße 
der Gnade und der leiden in Jesu 
D. Falcknern

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 136
Author: Falckner, Daniel
