Keywords: Newman 
Henry
London
England
SPCK
Notes: Bartlets Buildings in London, 24th June 1728
Rever'd Sirs,

When it had pleas'd GOD to take to himself the late Reverend and 
LEarned Mr. Professor Franck, his Removal from the Stage in which
the Providence of GOD had placed and so signally propser'd him, 
gave a universall Damp to all that wish'd well to themany pious 
and noble Designs he was engag'd in; but none were more deeply 
affected than the Society in England for PRomoting Christian 
Knowledge, who had long experienced by a most agreeable 
Correspondence with him,his unshaken and steady Resolution, by 
all prudent and possible Methods to advance the Glory of GOD, and
the Englargment of the Kingdom of our Dear Saviour in all Parts 
of the World, the most distant and barbarous not excepted.

Under so great a Concern it was a singular Consolation to the 
Society to be inform'd by Dr. Franck's Letter of the 10th of 
September last, that His Royal Majesty of Prussia had appointed 
Professor Franck's Son Gotthilf Augustus Franckiusand Mr. 
Freylinghusius Principal Directore of the Orphan House and all 
the other Institutions thereon depending, and that it had pleas'd
GOD to raise up two Persons so eminent for Piety and Learning 
long experienced in the Managment of so great a Trust, to supply 
a Loss that it was fear'd would be irreparable by the Death of 
the late excellent Professor.

The Sociey congratulate you both on the Honour of succeeding so 
great an Examplar, and pray GOD to direct and prosper your 
Administration with equal Success in all the Branches of the high
Trust repos'd in you: And the Society have unanimously chosen 
both of you Corresponding Members of their Body, desiring that 
you wouldalways with the same Freedom as your Predecessor did, 
demand their Assistance in whatever is in their Power for 
furthering all you excellent Designs, particularly in Relation to
the Protestant Mission to East India, which his Majesty the King 
of Denmark has so generously laid Foundation for at Tranquebar.

It is unnecessary for me to mention here what has been done by 
the Society in that Undertaking to you that are so well 
acquainted with all the Progress of it from the Beginning, it may
sufficeonly to assure you that the Society are resolv'd to 
continue their good Offices in Conjunction with yours for 
supporting a Design that promises so much Glory to Almighty GOD.

Mr. Schultze the PRincipal Missionary at Tranquebar has lately 
visited many of the European Settlements on the Coast of 
Coromandel, and porposes if one or more of the Missionaries were 
permitted to settle at Fort St. George, and other populaous 
Places, the Propagation of the Gospel would be more facilitated 
than by confining their Labour to Tranuebar and the parts 
adjacent. In regard to which, presuming upon theKing of 
Denmark's Approbation of such a Proposal, the Society have 
obtain'd fresh Assurances from teh English East INdia Company 
that the Missionaies shall always be protected in their 
Settlements, and the Society are taking Measures for encreasing 
the Supply which the Missionaires must necessarily want, when the
Bounds of their Vineyard shall be so much enlarg'd.

The Society desire your Acceptance of a Specimen of their Books 
such as in Pursuance of their Designs at Home they dipserse among
the Poor of this Kingdom, and they hope much Goodhas been done by
them, among which Books you will find a short Narrative of all 
the Designs the Society are at present engag'd in, together with 
an Account of several other Religious Societies in London, who 
are often mistaken one for the other expecially by Forreigners, 
but each of them have a distinct Province, and always confine 
themselves to the Business of it. Give me Leave only to mention 
that the Incoporated Society for Propagating teh Gospel in 
Foreign Parts are often taken for the Society for Promoting 
Christian Knowledge, and this Society for them; but in Truth they
are as distinct as East and West, the Incorporated Society being 
by their Charter limitted to the English Settlements in the West 
Indies, but the Society for Promoting Christian Knowledge being a
voluntary Body, are under no LImitation but the common Laws of 
Discretion, and therefore they extend their Acts? to the East 
Indies, and to any part of the World within reach of their 
Abilities.

I should have made this Address to you sooner, if I hd not been 
prevented by a tedious Indisposition, which I bless GOD is now in
a great Measure remov'd, and hope you will excuse my taking the 
liberty to write in English since as Mr. Ziegenhagen informs me, 
you understand it. But you may please to answer me in Latin or 
what other Language is most familiar to you.

May GOD Almighy prosper all your pious Endeavours for hi Glory; 
And let me particularly recommend it toyou, to pray to Almighty 
GOD for a Blessing on the Conultations and Endeavours of the 
Society forthe same End. I have the HOnour to be, Rever'd 
Gentlemen, Your most obedient and humbly devoted servant,
Henry Newman

PS: the Packets will be sent to you by the Way of Hamborough, or
as Mr. Ziegenhagen our porpetual Friend shall advise.
Language: English

Reference Type:  Generic
Record Number: 321
Author: Newman, Henry
Year: 1733
Title: London
Secondary Author: Francke, Gotthilf August and Freylinghausen
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1733/12/21
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/35:5 [10294]
England Fasc. II, s. 61/162; Halle: 30, 2; Film Nr. 20, 1035
Custom 1: 1733-12-21
Custom 2: 51.507351, -0.127758
Keywords: Newman Henry
Francke G A

London
England
Salzburgers
Notes: London, 21st Decr. 1733
Reverend Sir:

I received in due time Your most acceptable Leter of the 19th 
Novr. N.S. which being laid before the Society was read and heard
with that attention which is always given upon reading a Letter 
from Professor Franck.

In answer to the first part of it, the Society think themselves 
very much oblig'd to You and have ordered me to send their hearty
Thanks for the care You have taken to recommend to the Trustees 
for Georgia and to the Society, two Gentlemen wo well qualify'd 
for Mister and Catechict to the Saltzburgers in Georgia as Mssrs 
Bolzius and Gronau are represented to be
 
The Society have agreed to allow the Minister 50£ Sterl p. 
anno. and the Catechist 80. £ to commence from teh time of 
their departure from Hall and prevail'd with the Reverend Mr. 
Butjenter one of their Members to go down to the Port of Dover 
where teh Transport Shipnow lies to ee that they are provided 
with all necessaries particularly to advance to them Half a year 
of their Salaries and to present them with such Plate and other 
Furniture for theHoly Communion as could be got ready at so short
a Warning and also 20s. to each Person above 20. Years of age. 
10s. to every Saltzburger above 12. and under 20 Years old, 5 s.
to all under 12. Years of Age. One of the Trustees for Georgia 
was likewise sent to Dover on the part of their Corporation to 
welcome them to England and to see them provided wth all 
necessary accommodations on board the Ship Purysburg.

I answer to the latter part of your Letter about contributing 
towards building an Hospital in Prussia for old decrepid 
Saltzburgers, the Society entertain so high an esteem for every 
Proposal that comes from Professor Franck, that they heartily 
wish it were in their power to comply with this, but in the 
present Instance, it is with great regret that they direct me to 
inform You, that the principal Benefactors towards relieving the 
Saltzburgers have confin'd their Bounty to such of them as shall 
accept of a Settlement in Hist Majesty's Dominions in America, 
agreably to which, the Society have already engag'd to settle 
moer Saltzburgers in Georgia, than the Sums hitherto collected 
will enable them to do, notwithstanding the liberal assistance 
given by the Trustees for that New Colony out of theParliamentary
Fund towards defraying the charge of their transportaton.

you will easily be convinc'd of this when I acquaint You that the
Society have out of the Casual Benfaction for this Service at 
several times since March 1732. remitted to the Reverend Mr. 
Urlsperger at Augsburg £1482:4:6 Sterl. part of which has 
been apply'd towards relieving those Emigrants who went to 
Prussia; beside this, the Society have thought it incumbent on 
them to secure an effectual Provision for supporting a Minister, 
a Catechist, and Schoolmaster to those who have left their Native
Country and friends, for the sake of Religion by appropriating 
2000£ for that Service and they have accordingly lodg'd that 
sum in the Publick Funds. So that considering the charge of the 
present Transport of 40. what remains will not suffice to defray 
one third or perhaps one Quarter of the Expence of the number to 
compleat 300. which they have commission'd Mr. Urlsperger to 
collect, and send to Roterdam, where the Trustees for Georgia 
receive them at their Expence

But as in all Cases of this nature it cannot be foreseen what may
be the Extent of the charge accrewing to it the Society rely on 
the same good Disposition of their Contributors who have enabled 
them to go so far as they have, to raise such further supplies as
shall be necessary to accomplish the Design of making a good 
Settlement for these Emigrants in Georgia.

The Society congratulate You on the gracious reception his 
Majesty of Prussia has given you in your late Journey to Berlin 
GOD be prais'd for all the Effects of this Royal Bounty to your 
University and Orphan house and may they continue to make his 
virtues illustrious to all Posterity.

I am also to thank you in the name of the Society for all the 
charitable and liberal Remittances you have annually made in 
favour of the Protestant Mission to the East Indies particularly 
to the establishment at Madras which owes its Origin to that at 
Tranquebar. and both of them their beginning to Your most worthy 
Father whose Memory is dear to all good Christians.

I doubt not but Mr. Ziegenhagen has transmitted to you the many 
agreable accounts which come to my hands from the Missionaries of
both Establihments lat Summer which seem to promise a glorious 
Harvest in the age to come, and by order of the Society I am now 
preparing to send to them every thing they have desired, on a 
presumption of having leave so to do by the East India 
Companyhere.

The Rev'd Mr. Rodde at Nawa has earnestly recommended to the 
Society the promoting an Impression at Hall of Arndtius de vero 
Christianismo in the Russian Language, by Russian Types in your 
PRinting House, presented many years ago by good Mr. Ludolph 
Secretary to Prince George of Denmark. The Society would be glad
to have your Opinion of that Proposal and whereabouts may be the 
charge of an Edition of 1000. Copies, and the difference of that
and 2000. Copies and whether You will not think a Book of less 
Bulk and Expence more proper.

I am Reverend and Dear Sir, Your most obliged humble Servant 
Henry Newman

My humble service to yr fellow Labourer Mr. Freylinghausen upon 
whose recovery from a fit of Apoplexy I heartily congratulate him
and you.

Record Number: 322
Author: Newman, Henry
Year: 1735
Title: London

Secondary Author: Members, SPCK
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1735/05/08
Type of Work: Circular Letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/35:7 [10296]
England Fasc. II, s. 61/162; Halle: 30, 1; Film nr. 20, 1042

Custom 1: 1735-05-08
Custom 2: 51.507351, -0.127758
Keywords: Newman Henry
Francke G A
London
England
SPCK

Saltzbergers
Notes: London, Bartlett's Building, Holborn;

It is Four Years since the SOCIETY for PRomoting Christian 
Knowledge, sent a Circular Letter to their Subscribing and 
Corresponding Members; which Delay has been occasion'd, in great 
measure, by Variety of more than ordinary Business, as will 
partly appear by the Abstracts of their Proceedings, annex'd to 
the Two last Anniversary Sermons preach'd at St. Sepulchre's, and
in the following Account.

As to the Protestant Mission in the East-Indies:

The Reverend Mr. John Anthony Sarorius, was sent over to Madras 
as an Assistant Missionary to Mr. Schultze; since which the 
Mission has been enlarg'd, by sending the Reverend Mr. John 
Earnest Geister, of the University of Hall, recommended by the 
very Worthy Mr Professor Franck. He arrived at Madras, to the 
great Joy of his Collegues, July 16. 1732. O.S.

These Three Worthy Missionaries go on (by the Blessing of GOD) 
very successfully, notwithstanding the Trouble of making 
themselves Masters of new Languages, and translating several 
Books; and the Difficulties they meet with, by a constant 
Opposition from Papists. This last Year, above Fifty Proselytes 
from Heathenism have been well Instructed, and received into 
their Church. They have begun to Educate Girls, as well as Boys;
and the Number of Both in the Malabarian and Portugueze Schools, 
is Forty Six. Of which Twenty two are cloath'd and fed by the 
Charity of a Worthy Gentleman in London, who as been a very 
liberal Benefactor to this Mission. The Missionaries have near 
finished a Translation of the BIBLE in the Gentou Language; which
if printed and dispersed, at least the New Testament, might be a 
means of communicating the Gospel, thro' many Parts of the Great 
Mogul's Empire.

THE Missionaries were in great Distress, for want of a convenient
Habitation; being provided with only One House, wherein each 
Missionary has but one small Room for Lodging, Furniture, and 
Books; and which House has hitiherto serv'd instead of a Church,
and Schools. To remedy this Inconvenience, which endanger'd 
their Healths, frm the Heat of the Climate, and the pernicious 
Insects which infest those hot Countries. The SoCIETY have 
lately made Application to the Honourable DIRECTORS of the 
EAST-INDIA COMPANY to grant Leave for the Building of a CHURCH, 
and Two School-Houses; which they have very generously been 
pleased to comply with. And the 4th of February last, the 
SOCIETY gave Directions to their MISSIONARIES to lay the 
Foundation of a Church of 40 Feet square; so contriv'd, that it 
may be enlarg'd to such Dimensions as shall be found necessary. 
And the SOCIETY have wrote at the same time to their 
Correspondents of the Council at Fort St. George, and the Two 
Chaplains there, to assist them with their Advice and Directions 
in carrying on the Building. And it was further recommended to 
them, that nothing be aim'd at but Durableness and Usefulness; 
avoiding all unnecessary Expence. The Worthy Gentleman 
beforemention'd, who has been a bountiful Contributor to this 
Mission, has sent over by the last Ships to the Value of 140£
and Professor Franck, of Hall in Saxony and Others, by the Hands 
of the Reverend Mr. Ziegenhagen, 200£. Both which Sums are 
sent to the Missionaries, towards Building the Church, etc.  But
as this Sum will come short of the Estimate of the Expence 
ofthese Buildings, te Society rust that Providence will raise up 
Benefactors, to compleat so noble and glorious a Design.

AN Overture being made of settling a New Mission at Fort St. 
Davi's, (an English Settlement between Fort St. George and 
Tranquebar) the Society very much approv'd of the PRoposal; 
looking upon it, as a hopeful Prosepct of enlarging the Church of
CHRIST, and spreading its saving Influence amongst the Indians: 
Accordingly, they have directed the Rev. Mr. Schultze to 
undertake the Charge of this Mission, as his Name is well known 
among theHeathens; as He is experienc'd in the Language and 
Manners of the People; and as his long Labours at Tranquebar, and
in the Mission at Madras, have, by the Divine Blessing, been so 
signally prosper'd.

The Society have already expended in the Purchase of the 
MIssion-House, and BurialGround, 408£ (including Benefactions
here, from Germany, and at Fort St. George) and are besides 
subject to a constant Expence, which, one Year iwth anotoher, 
amounts to upwards of 360£ As the SOCIETY'S Fund is not at 
present sufficient for these good purposes, and as the Expence 
will now be increased, by the extraordinary Charges which will 
necessarily arise from extending the Mission; the SOCIETY 
heartily recommend This Branch of their Designs, to all Those who
wish for the Enlargement of the Kingdom of JESUS CHRIST upon 
Earth.

THO' the Society have engag'd for the Support of the English 
Mission at Fort St. Goerge, beyond their present Abilities; yet 
They have madethe usual Remittances to the Danish Missionaries at
Tranquebar of Paper, and other Utensils fo the Printing PRess, 
and Apohecar's Shop. An Account of their present State and 
Prosperity, will be printed in an Abstract, at the End of the 
next Anniversary Sermon at St. Sepulchre's.

As ot the Impression of the New testament and Psalter in Arabick 
--- The Society's Correspondent at Aleppo, acquaints them, That 
He had lately sent 200 new Testaments, 200 Psalters, and 100 
Compendiums of Christian Doctrine, to Consul Barton, as a Present
to the Grek Patriarch at Alexandria; and more will be sent, when 
desired. By letters from the Rev. Mr. Ludolph Trefurt, Minister 
of the German Lutheran Congregation at Petersburg, to the Rev. 
Dr. Guerdes in London, the SOCIETY is inform'd; That H had 
receiv'd several Arabick New Testaments and Psalters, from teh 
Rev. Mr. Rodde, tehir Correspondent at Narva; part of which He 
had putinto the Hands of Mr. Von Hochmuht, who promised to 
disperse them in several Parts of Persia. And part ino the Hands
of a Clergyman, who is gone with an Officer sent by the Czarina 
on an Expedition to Kampschatka, the furthest Country towards the
North-East, beyond Siberia. The rest are reserved in the 
SOCIETY's Store, to be sent to such Places, at such Times and in 
such Numbers as shall be thought most adviseable.

The SOCIETY earnestly recommend to their Members, the visiting of
the WORK-HOUSES in their Neighourhoods, and pressing the daily 
Usse of Prayers out of the Liturgy; together with a Prayer at the
End of the last printed Account of the Work-houses.

The SOCIETY cannot omit renewing their Request to their Members, 
frequently to visit the Charity Schools in their Neighbourhoods; 
and to recommend, that with Religious Instructions, they should 
join all proper Methods of inuring the Children to Labour and 
Industry, and of Instructing them in a true Sense of their great 
Obligations to be Dutiful and Loyal to the present happy 
Protestant Government. And whereas it is justly apprehended, 
that the Popish Emissaries that flock in amongst us from Abroad, 
will endeavour (as they have already attempted upon some of the 
Scholars of a publick Grammar-School inthis City) to poison the 
weak Minds of these poor Children. It is therefore hoped, that 
Those who have the Care of the several Charity-Schools, will 
direct the Schoolmaters, to give their Children a just Impression
of the abominable Corruptions, Idolatry, and cruel Persecutions 
of Popery.

Upon an Informaton and Petition of the Lorad Primate, 
Archbishops, Bishops, NOblemen,and Gentry o the Kingdom of 
Ireland to His Majesty,  setting forth the Increase of Poery and
Disaffecton to the present Establishment there; proceeding in a 
great measure from the gross Ignorance the People are kept in by 
the Popish Clergy; and that the proper Way, thro' GOD'S 
Blessing, for cnverting and civilizing the said deluded People, 
and bringing them in time to be good Christians, and faithful 
Subjects, would be to errect and establish a sufficient Number of
English Protestant Schools, wherein the Children of the Irish 
Natives may be Instructed in the English Tongue and the 
Fundamental Principles of True Religion. His Majesty was 
therefore Graciously pleased to grant his ROYAL CHARTER for 
Erecting such Schools; which was opened the 6th of February, 
1733. And from the known Zeal and Prudence of those worthy 
Prelates, Noblemen, and Gentlemen, who have undertaken the 
Government and Direction of these Schools, itis not at all to be 
dobted, but by the Blessing of GOD, Success will attend their 
pious Endeavours.

The Society does not doubt but it will be a particular Pleasure 
to all their Members, to hear of the Increase and Prosperity of 
the Orphan-House at Hall; from whence the Society have been 
suply'd with many worthy Missionaries; By an Account sent from 
Professor Franck to an Honourable Member of the SOCIETY in 
London, dated in November last, it appears, that there are in the
German School, 1600. In the Latin School, 506. In the Royal 
Collegiate School, 71. Masters teaching in these Schools, 182. 
Students in the Seminary for Schoolmasters, 33. Inspectors, 8. 
In all, 2400. Above 800 of which are maintain'd in the 
Orphan-House; for whose Support the Mercy of GOD has hitherto 
afforded all Necessaries. thus has the Almighty from very small 
Beginnings raised this Orphan-House, to enable them not only to 
educate some Thousands of poor Children, but also several 
students of Divinity. Some upon their Travels through different 
Parts of Germany, Poland, Holland, and england, to convert 
theJews. Some with the Saltzburgers in Georgia; Some at 
Tranquebar; and Others at Fort St. Goerge: All proving, under 
GOD, useful Labourers in his Vineyard.

IN the Beginning of the Year 1732. the SOCIETY, when they heard 
the very melancholly Account of the cruel Sufferings of the 
PRotestants in the Archbishoprick of Saltzburg, (having first 
obtain'd his MAJESTY's gracious Permission) resolv'd upon doing 
all that lay in their Power to raise Collections for these their 
greatly Persecuted Brethren. Accordingly they published Two 
Accounts of their Sufferings; which moved many charitable and 
pious Persons to contribute liberally to their Relief. About 
1500£ of those Collections were remitted to Germany for the 
Relief of many THousand poor Saltzburgers, forced out of their 
native Country in the depth of a very cold Winter, destitute even
of common Necessaries, before it was known whither They were to 
go. Above twice as much was reserv'd for the Assistance of such 
amongst them as were desirous of accepting a Settlement in His 
Majesty's New-erected Colony of Georgia; where Land is allotted 
for the Benefit of such as are persecuted for the sake of the 
Gospel, (in so happy a Climate, and a Soil so fruitful, as may 
make them some Amends for what they were obliged to leave in 
their own Country) Accordingl, 45 Men, Women, and Children, with
Mr. Von Reck their Commissary, sailed from the Downs the 8th of 
January, 1733-4 and arrived at Georgia the 7th of March 
following. An Account of their Voyage, and happy Settlement in 
that Province, appears in an Extract lately printed, of the 
Journals of Mr. Commissary Von Reck, who conducted the first 
Transport of Saltzburgers to Georgia, and of the Reverend Mr. 
Bolzius, one of their Ministers.

THESE Accounts of the kind REception of their Countrymen, 
encourag'd more of these poor persecuted People, who had before 
left their Country, to follow them to Gerogia. And accordingly, 
58 Men, women, and a few Children, with Mr. Vat their Conductor, 
sailed from the Downs the 8th of November, in Company with the 
Indian Chiefs, returning to their own Country. And the SOCIETY 
have within these few Days, with great Pleasure received an 
Account of their happy and safe Arrival, in prefect Health, the 
28th of December following. And they thankfully acknowledge the 
Protection of the Almighty, that these two Embarktions have been 
perform'd in themidst of Winter, in so short a time, and without 
any Misfortune.

THE Money at that Time remaining in the Hands of the Trustees for
that Charity (exclusive of a Sum placed in the publick 
Securities, as a Fund for the Payment of the Salaries tothe 
ministers and Schoolmaster, till such time as a settled Provision
can be made for them) was not near sufficient to discharge the 
Demands made upon them, viz. For their Expences in theri long 
Journey from Augsburg to Rotterdam, and their Passage from thence
to Gravesend; for their Subsistence whilst in England; for their 
Voyage to Georgia; their Maintenance there for One Year; and for 
Arms, Utensils and other necessary Provisions. But it pleased 
GOD to move the Hearts of many truly Pious and Charitable 
Persons, to send in their seasonable and liberal Contributions, 
so that the SOCIETY are enabled to defray the Expences of the 
last Transpot: And They hope the same kind Disposition will 
continue, towards the Assistance of many more of these greatly 
injured and indigent People, should they offer themselves to go 
to Georgia; which 'tis highly probable tey will when theyhear of 
the kind Reception, and good Settlement their Countrymen have 
already met with there.

WHILE the Society's Thoughts were taken up for the relief of 
Those that suffer'd for the sake of the Protestant Religion in 
Foreign Parts, they were justly alarm'd at the extraordinary 
Endeavours and Artifices of the Priests of teh Church o Rome, in 
making Converts to Popery in our own Country. OUR RIGHT REVEREND
AND WORTHY DIOCESAN, ever vigilant over the People committed to 
his Charge, has ltely wrote a Circular Letter to his Clergy; 
"Exhorting Them to use the greatest Diligence in watching 
Thosewho lay in wait to deceive and to spare no Pains in hindring
their People from falling into a Snare; that is, from being 
peverted to a Religion, which has so grossly corrupted the true 
Faith and Doctrine of Christ, and introduced so much Superstition
and Idolatry into the Christian Worship." The CONVOCATION 
have also lately taken notice of the Growth of Popery, in their 
Address to His MAJESTY; WHO was graciously pleased to commend 
their Zeal in suppressing It, and assures Them, "THAT NOTHING 
SHALL BE WANTING ON HIS PART, TO GIVE THEIR ENDEAVOURS THE 
DESIRED EFFECT."

THE SOCIETY would not be wanting at this important Juncture, to 
do what lies intheir Power to furnish proper Antidotes for the 
Poison so artfully prepared, and dispers'd with such uncommon 
Diligence. And They have accordingly appointed a COMMITTEE to 
consider what Tracts it will be necessary to Reprint, and to add 
them to a great many good ones they already have in their 
CATALOGUE, against the pernicious Errors of the Church of Rome. 
And the SOCIETYwould be glad to know from time to time from their
Members, what Arts are made use of, and what Books dispersed by 
Popish Emissaries, in order to pervert and draw the Unwary from 
teh Simplicty that is in CHRIST JESUS.

THE SOCIETY have great Reason to fear, that the too general 
Omission of Family-Worship, and of Catechising Children and 
servants in the Fundamental principles of the Christian Religion,
together with the great and notorious Neglect of the Publick 
Worship of Almighty GOD; The profane Treatment of Divine 
Revelation, and the Author of our Salvation Himself, in Deistical
Books and Pamphlets, (so serviceable to the Popish Interest, and 
so agreeable to the Popish Maxms) have very much contributed to 
the late extraodinary Progress of POPERY, which sensibly affects 
every true Protestant. The SOCIETY therefore earnestly 
recommends it to their Members, and all others that have a 
serious Regard for Religion, to use their warmest Endeavours upon
so important an Occasion, by all proper Methods to bring People 
to a greater Love for their BIBLES, and a just Sense of the 
Necessity there is to begin the good Work of Religion in private 
Families To engage their Housholds to come constantly to Church,
and seriously observe the Lord's Day; in order to fix in their 
Minds a due Regard for Religion, and give them a Love and Zeal 
for the Protestant Faith. For this Purpose, the SOCIETY 
recommends the dispersing, together with the Tracts against 
POPERY, such other Pieces in their Catalogue, as prove the Diine 
Authority and Excellence of theHoly Scriptures; and such as shew 
the Necessity and Advantages of Private, Family, and PUblick 
Worship.

By order of the Society the foregoing account of their 
Proceedings is sent by 

Revd. Sr. Your most humble servent,
Henry Newman
London 8. May 1735

NB: To prevent Mistakes, our Benefactors are desired to take 
Notice, that the Name of this Voountary Society is, The society 
for the Promoting Christian Knowledge.

The SOCIETY have agreed to reprint the Plausible Arguments of a 
Romish Priest from Scripture and Antiquity, Answered By Dr. 
COMBER: Which their Members may have on the usual terms.

Language: English

Notes: London 6 June 1735
Reverend Sir

I receiv'dyour most acceptable letter of the 21st of May last 
N.S. by our excellent friend Mr. Ziegenhagen in answer to the 
enquiry he was desir'd to make of the power vvested in the 
Missionaries at Tranquebar to confer Orders on such Persons among
the Malabarian Converts to Christianity as shall be found fitly 
qualify'd for Divine Offices, particularly the administration of 
the Holy Sacraments.

A Translation of your letter was read at the last General Meeting
of the Society which happen'd to be a full one and they 
unanimously express'd their entire satisfaction at the Account 
you gave of that Affair, and have order'd me to put them in mind 
of giving their directions at the next return of the Ships to 
India for preventing any disputes or misunderstandings, that may 
hereafter grow in those parts upon a supposition of the Holy 
Orders confer'd in India not being Valid.

We daily expect further & more ample Accounts of the progress of 
the Missions both at Tranquebar and Madras, teh prosperity of 
which is under GOD ery much owing to yor. charitable and generous
Sollicitation in Germany, concerning which a short printed 
Account ins herewith sent, together with some other little tracts
lately imported into the Society store, which they desire your 
acceptance of by Reverend and Dear Sr,
Your most obliged humble Servant Henry Newman

Notes: Bartlet's Buildings, London, 27t June 1735
Reverend & Dear Sir,
The Society being desirous to redress as much as they can what 
has been long the complaint of wise and good men, viz. the 
Reading of Profane Heathen Authors in Grammar Schools, and to 
introduce the use of Christian Authors in their Stead for the 
instructions of Youths in the Latin and Greek Languages, I am 
order'd to request you would be pleas'd toinform the Society what
Latin and Greek Authors are read in teh Padagogium at Glaucha.

The Society daily expect further advices from teh Missionaries in
East India with letters for you, which shall be convey'd as soon 
as possible.

I again thank you for your favour of the 21st of May by the hands
of Mr. Ziegenhagen, the contents of which I acquainted you by a 
letter of teh 6th Curt by mr. Jacobi was very acceptable to the 
Society, who gladly receive any advices from you as a hearty 
friend and zealous Promoter of all their Designs.

Give me leave to assure you that I am with all possible respect
Reverend & Dear Sir
Your most Obedient Humble Servants, Henry Newman
My Humble serivce to Mr. Freylinghausen

London
SPCK
Notes: London 15th August 1735
Reverend Sr
I receiv'd your great favour of the 28th of July last N.S. and 
thank you for it in the name of the Society, but having expressed
my self ambiguously in the first Paragraph of my letter of the 
27th of June in the following words:
"The Society being desirous to redress as much as they can 
what has long been the complaint of wise and Good Men, Viz. the 
Reading of Profane Heathen Authors in Grammar Schools and to 
introduce the use of Christian Authors in their stead for the 
Instruction of Youth in the Latin and Greek Languages:"

It is my Duty to acquaint you that it is not the present design 
of the Society to exclude all heathen Authors out of Grammar 
Schools, but only the most Profane which might endanger the 
Morals of those who are instructed out of them, and lesen it not 
obliterate that Reverence to GOD and Sacred Things which cannot 
be too early or strongly inculcated into outhfull Minds.

Be pleas'd therefore to let the Revd. Mr. Freyer know this with 
any other Gent. that may have misapprehended the intent of my 
letter

I am Reverend Sr.
Your most obed. humble Servant
Henry Newman

The Ships daily expected from E. India are not yet arrived.

Language: English

Notes: Bartlet's Buildings, London, 5th Sept. 1735

Reverend Sir,
The Society for Promoting Christian Knowledge observing with 
pleasure how much the Oriental Languages flourish in your Schools
and Universities and being desirous to encourage the same in 
Ours, do beg the Favour of you to acquaint them what Methods are 
taken to oblige the Young Students to learn those Languages; And 
particularly whether it is insisted on as a Qualification for 
Degrees or for Holy Orders, or for both, or if there be any other
method in use amongst You which by experience you find most 
effectual please to communicate it to,

Reverend Sr, 
Your most Obedient humble Servant,
Henry Newman

PS: The Society would be glad to be inform'd of the Moethods 
used at Jena as well as Hall for encouraging the Study of the 
Hebrew and other Oriental Languages.

I immediately convey'd to Mr. Ziegenhagen all the Letters for 
Germany, which came lately to my hands from teh Missionaries in 
East India. My humble service to the Rev. Mr. Freylinhausen

Georgia
Ziegenhagen
Notes: Bartlet's Buildings
London, 2 May 1740
Reverend Sir
I had the honur of your Letter of the 14th of November last by 
Mr. Kiernander and acquainted the Society with the Contents, who 
have ordered me to thank you for recommending a person of his 
Merit to the Service of the Mission at Cudulore where theyhope it
may please God to make him a happy Instrument of propagating 
Christian Knowledge for many years among the Heathen in 
conjunction with Mr. Geister who has earnestly desir'd such an 
Assistant might be sent to him.

He embark'd with his Fellow Travellers Messieurs Fabriius and 
Leghlin on bord the Colchester Capt. Michlefield; the last Letter
I had from him was dated at Spithead 9th of April when they were 
all well, perparing to sail for India, not a little pleas'd with 
the civilities of their Captian; By the Society's Order and Mr. 
Ziegenhagen's good offices, I hope they were accommodated with 
every thing tthey could want in so long a voyage. They sail'd 
soon after under a convoy of several Men of War till they should 
be clear of any Visit from the Spaniards on the Ocean, and I hope
God will protect them from every danger to which they are liable 
iin so long a Voyage.

George William Beck a Native of Cudulore will I hope have the 
honour to present you with this; Mr. Ziegenhagen will inform you
by what Providence he has been sent under your Protection, where 
I hope he may grow to be a usefull Man, and become in time 
capable of serving his Native Country if it should please God he 
ever return thither.

At the desire of Mr. Ziegenhagen I have had the plesure of his 
company ever since his arrival in England till the hard Winter 
would permit his embarking for Germany, inwhich time he has given
proofs of his being bless'd with a happy Genius capable of 
excellent Improvemt. which I hope it will please God to give him 
Grace to make a right use of under the Opportunities he may enjoy
by your direction in germany. Mr. Geister has I doubt not given 
an Account of his Baggage, the remains of which excepting what 
was worn out in hi Voyage, are now sent with him under the care 
of Mr. Welch.

The Society are under many obligations to you for the favours you
have conferr'd onthe Mission at Madras and Cudulore, and have 
always desir'd Mr. Ziegenhagen to signify their Thanks to you for
them; give me leave to desire your acceptance of aRepetition of 
their acknowledgments, and of a small Packet of such things as 
have been publish'd by them for 2. or 3. years past on the 
Subject of the Mission and other Things, for the Service of 
Religion.

I must also acknowledge your kind present of Arndt's True 
Christianity in the Russian Language, which Mr. Ziegenhagen 
lately gave in your name to the Soicety's Library and he was 
desired to thank you for it. I have just now Letters from 
Georgia where the missionaries are well and I hope have given you
an Account of their Welfare under cover to Mr. Ziegenhagen to 
whom I have sent a large Packet. Both Indies feel the effects of
your charitable influence from Halle; May that illustrius 
Seminary under your Care, continue to furnish faithfull ministers
to the Church of God to the end of Time, and may you always have 
cause to rejoyce in the Success of your indefatigable Labours is 
the wish of Revereend and Most Honoured Sir, Yor. most Obedient 
Humble Servant, Henry Newman
To themost Revd. Mr. Professor Franck
Language: English

Notes: London, 16 March 1741-42
Reverend Sir
My last to you was of the 2nd of May 1740 in answer to your 
obliging Letter of the 14th November prceding by Mr. Kiernander, 
of whose sfe arrival in East India I doubt not but you have long 
since been inform'd by Letters from himself and his Colleague at 
Cudulore, between whom there seems to be a happy Harmony 
presaging that success to the Mission which their Friends in 
Europe wish for.

Mr. Ziegenhagen long ago acquainted the Society with your 
Benefaction of £100 to that Mission, and of £10 from 
otoher Benefactors for which he was desir'd to return the Thanks 
of the Society, and theMissionaries themselves having since 
inform'd them of the Receipt not only of those Benefactions, but 
of several Books to the Mission Library at Cudulore convey'd by 
your order from Tranquebar I am to request you would accept the 
Thanks of the Society for them.

At the desire of these Missionaries a copy of their Journal in 
English 1740 has been made and sent to Mr. Ziegenhagen to be 
transmitted to you to which I have now added a copy of the 
Iconography of the Mission house at Cuculore herewith sent.

Mr. Schultze at Fort St. George has desir'd an Assistant 
Missionary may be sent to him at Madras but as theSociety are not
in a Condition to grant that at present they have contented 
themselves with obtaining leave from the illustrious College at 
Copenhagen that one of their Missionaries at Tranquebar go to 
Madras whenever Mr. Schultze shall withdraw himself from the 
Service of the Mission there, (of whcih he has given intimations 
by another hand) and to take Care for the Support of its interest
till the Society can be advis'd in the propoerest means for the 
future conduct of it, wherein I am sure they will be glad of that
prudent advice and assistance which you are always ready to give.

The late and present commotions in Germany must have been fatal 
to many seats for the advancement of Religion and Learning, 
butHall and Glaucha seem to have hitherto escap'd the desolation 
of War, and the Socity hope the same gracious Providence which 
has founded & to this day wonderfully bless'd that Seal of 
Religion & Learning the Orphanhouse will still continue to make 
it prosperous as it has been for the Service of true Religion, 
not only in Europe and the remotest parts of Asia, but in wild 
America, and if it be not asking too great a favour the Society 
wouldbe glad to be inform'd of the present state of the Orphan 
house, & its dependencies, particularly that you would prevail 
with Mr. Professor Callenberg to favour them with some account of
the Success of his Endeavours to perswade the Jews to read the 
Gospel, and to mbrace their & the Christians true Messiah.

I ought when I ask so great a favour as this to send you some 
Account of the progress of the Society here which I promise God 
willing to do, whenever Mr. Ziegenhagen shall be so kind as to 
inform me of an opportunity of sending what cannot conveniently 
be sent by the Post.

May the Effects of your Labours for the Glory of God, and the 
enlargement of theKingdom of our Blessed Saviour upon Earth, be 
as extensive as the uttermost parts of this Globe and as lasting 
as time itself are the wishes of the Society as well as of 
Reverend and most hOnoured Sir, Yor. most obedient humble 
servant,
Henry Newman

PS: It will be a pleasure to me to be inform'd whether you have 
wrote to me since your letter by Mr. Kiernander to be satisfy'd 
that none of your agreable letters to the Society or me have 
miscarry'd when you honour me with a letter I shall be glad to 
hear what is become of George William Beck and wether he is 
design'd ever to return to his friends in Est India?
Language: English

Reverend Sr.
I am sorry to hear of your indisposition by our good friend Mr. 
Ziegenhagen. i shall be glad to hear it has pleas'd God to 
restore your health.

I hope you receiv'd my letter of the 16th of March last wherein I
promis'd to sendyou and Professor Callenberg an Account of the 
progress of teh Society here by the 1st opportunity which I 
gladly now embrace by the Son of Professor Michaelis towhich are 
added some other things lately brought into the Society's Store 
according to the List enclosed.

I shall be oblig'd to you to make my complements to the Rev'd Mr.
Professor Callenberg and to pray his acceptance of the packet now
sent from the Society, and if I can save so much time as to write
to him by this opporutnity I shall be glad being his and Reverend
Sr. yor most obedt. humble servt.
Henry Newman

PS: I have just now letters from East India of Sept. last, with 
packets for Mr. Ziegenhagen, wherein I doubt not are letters for 
you, which I have forwarded to him without loss of Time.

Author: Parsons, Thomas
Year: 1713
Title: Halle
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1713/01/16
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/38:1
Custom 1: 1713-01-16
Custom 2: 51.496979, 11.968803
Notes: Most Reverend 
Sr.
I rather accus than excuse this my bold writing: but because I 
was afraid to be to troublesome to You with my presence, I chose 
to do that in a letter what I shoud by rights in presence. You 
should know Revernd Sr that the design why I was sent to Hall 
was, that I shou'd return again for London, not as I came out 
thither, but prepared to serve God & my Nighbour. But that can't
be done in the best with these chool studies, shich have hitherto
occupied my mind & industry for about six years and a half; 
(though I won't deny that they are usefulin their kind) yet every
one will iudge, that the Acadmical studies, unto which the others
are but subornal, can fit & prepare such a one as I ammuch better
to fulfil the desire of my HOnoured Patrons, & to serve my 
Neighbor but especially bring one unto a better understanding of 
the divine word & per consequens how one shall aright care for 
his own soul, as being the sole reason why we are born. Now, 
Reverend Sr, you seeing the pure affect at my petition, that it 
don't proceed out of an aspiring Spirit, I hope you will likewise
be pleased to grant what I desire: it being this, that because 
at Easter you are wonted to demitt some schollars out of the 
Superior form, to reward their industry, unto the University, 
likewise to lett me partake of the same benefit. The reasons I 
have partly alledged allready, unto which we might yet add this 
that I don't know when it might please my Honoured Patrons to 
call me back, & would there fore before I depart from Hall 
willingly see what they do in the University, and at least have a
pragustum of those studies. I cou'd alledge many more reasons, 
if I were not afraid to be too troublesome unto You with many 
words, I hope that these, which I have set down, will suffice, 
because I know that you yourself perceive it to be necessary more
then I You will, Reverend Sr., if you permitt what I desire, not 
only oblige me to you more & more, but likewise his studies 
promote, whom I am perswaded You care for & make me,
remain Reverend Sr, your ever obedient client at Command,
Thomas Parsons
ad xv cal. febr. cbbccxiii
Language: English

Reference Type:  Generic
Record Number: 239
Author: Parsons, Thomas
Year: 1713
Title: Halle
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1713/08/19
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 30/38:2
Custom 1: 1713-08-19
Custom 2: 51.496979, 11.968803
Notes: Most Reverend 
Sr.
As I hear & perceive some body or other has been a telling you 1.
that I had drawn my sword in ye City. 2. that I had been in ye 
princes Garden very often, & taken nosegays & said they were holy
as being made of a young woman. 3. that as Mr. Schwabhäuser 
has been out of town I were always used to come very late home. 
But Sr. may it please you to read these few lines which I hear 
lay before your Eyes, not to excuse myself, as if I were quite 
innocent in this whole matter, or to vituperate those, who have 
done me this kindness, as to tell you, that I might by you be 
brought to a better mind, no not in the least; but only to beg 
favour of you, & that it might please to think a little on my 
oung years, which in ye beginning of haveing a little liberty 
more than ordinary, most commonly run into one excess or other, 
not knowing how to lag reins upon their fervent heat; & that 
especially when they are deceived as well by the examples of 
others, as likewise by ye provocation & advice of a fondling 
friend; but as for those points which are laid to my charge, & 
especialyl concerning the first; I know not wether it has been 
done or no; of ye two last points I find my self fully guilty 
wihtout any excuse at all, & without any exception Do therefore, 
Most Rev'd Sr. desire nothing else, then only that it may please 
you, to let this my wicked abhorred, abominable & detestable 
behaviour be forgotten, and blotted out of all Remembrance; but 
this I don't beg as if, when having got pardon I did design to go
on in such a wicked course of life; but I rather vow & promise 
before God to behave my self so in the future as I may be 
pleasing to God & men; whereunto I hope God of his infinite 
goodness & mercy will be pleased to give me grace & to purge my 
soul from all filthy lust & desires, from all petualnt actions, &
to make a useful vessel in his house! THus recommending my self 
to your favour; I remain
most reverend sr
Your forever bounden client
Thomas Parsons
ss. theol. st
Hall ye 19 Aug. 1713
Language: English

Notes: Immanuel!
Mein in demselbigen vielgelibter bruder.

Ich habe nun Zwey mahl auf offentlicher Post an der Hr. Wynant? 
Töllner geschriben den ich in den ein Brieffe einen Briff an 
einen Studiohuren Theologia nacher Freyberg geleget, und 
gebethen, er Mögte doch den Hr. Oessinger, so zu Halle sein 
soll, bitten ihn zu beßtel. bey den andern Brieff habe ich 
die Apologie für den H. Töllner gesand so mir von den Hr.
Paston zu Schermer eingeliefert war, habe aber auff keines 
nachricht erhalten. Itzo sende einen Brief so von Utrecht an 
mich gesand ist, worauf ich so viel von Hr. Lott Fischer sehr 
daß der Hr Gichtel den Brieff must unterschlagen haben, weil 
aber einige dinge darinnen, daran um und andern geleg, also 
wollen doch in Ihn setzen durch Hr. Schermer, daß der Brief 
zur vorschlein komme, ? Hr Lott Fischer überantwartet were. 
Es ist zwar eine muhe aber die es woll welche ist das neidische 
haß? ist in Gichel, das habe ich wohl gestuchet? daraus, 
welches nicht gut ist. Habe auch neulich an den l. Newer? 
geschriben, das der ulrich der Papsel? ? des Päkgen geldes 
hir vergeßen habe, es kan nur auff unser conto geschrieben 
werden gegen wertigen armer studiosen, deßen vatter ein 
secretarius, ? abgebrant ist mit andern bey ? ? bringet diese 
Brief schließet ein guter mensch, kan er allgemählig zur 
informitiren den hinder ? werden so thun sie ? einen dienst womit
den ewig liebe christi ? ? ?

treuer
J. Wilhelm Petersen
Niedendodeleben
1699 den 8 marty

ps des H. Prof. Francke Brieff habe zu recht auf den meinigen 
erhalten. Habuta ? in latin!

Notes: Niederndodeleben, den 23 Juni 1699
Imanuel

In demselben sowerther freund und bruder

dem gelibten zeilen haben woll in htig? erhalten aber noch nicht 
wieder schreiben können, auß mangel der zeit, und 
geschicken, daß daß gelt richtig Empfangen ist mir ser 
liebe, waß aber Ibrig sein solten, ist mir nicht bewust woll 
aber, daß wan rechte Zinse geben nach Waß mangelte, 
welches nach zu erstatt hoffen, in desen danke nochmallen 
hertzlich vor alle Erwisenen liebe So ihmes orths gemassen, auch 
davor daß sie mich wider sehen möchten, worzu auf meiner 
seyd, noch kein auß kommen dazu sehen kann, auß mangel 
der Zeit. Und gelegenheit, ob ichs woll ser wünschte und 
auch groß benötiget bin, von im und auf rathes zu Hallen,
mein dochter ist vergangen wochen bey mir gewesen, halten wieder 
an im nun reise ich mit wegen zu mein schwager zu thun Wir 
bericht eß mich aber ankommen weit so ich muß kann ich 
nicht berichten, gott gebe mir gnad und gedult dazu, wan selbst 
zu gegen wunde sich ohne zweifel ein meines zu andern als 
schreiben finden? gott geben eß wanß sein will, daß 
wir ein ander zu sprechen kommen. Unser leute sind schon 5 
wochen auß, und bekammen Keine? brieffe von sie Weiß 
nicht wo sie sein oder wan sie woll wieder kommen, die liebe 
mamma hat mich zum schülerin ihr ihm hauße gemacht, und 
hat mir ihn hauß an verthraut? wan mirs mir guth machen 
könte, gern wolten weiß thun Ich bin woll jederman zu d?
verbinden, wan nur duchdig wenn? doch ???

PS: bitte alle kinder gottes hertzlichen grüß ob ich 
schon nicht dar und selden schreiben werden sie mein doch nicht 
vergesen, welches wünsche mein analisel grüset auch 
hertzl, spricht der ????? too hard to read!

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 142
Author: Rost, Gottfried
Year: 1702
Title: Halle
Secondary Author: Neubauer, Georg Heinrich
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1702/10/17
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 18,2/11:7 [6470]
Custom 1: 1702-10-17
Custom 2: 51.496979, 11.968803
Notes: This 
section is included in a series of reports written to Neubauer 
when Francke was in Berlin (presumably Neubauer was there too) 
re: what was going on at Halle.

Halle den 17. Oct. 1702
Nach prandir

Wehrtester Herr Neubauer
Weiß nicht, ob Ihn mein letztes nach gestern in Berlin wird 
angetroffen haben: wo nicht, weird es der H. Baron von Kanstein 
nach senden daß Er es zu Magdeburg bekommt hiebey sende nach 
unterschiedene Briefe; kan sie der Herr Prof. unter weges nicht 
lesen, mag es zu Halle geschehen. Herrn M. Hermschmidts Brief 
kan der Herr Prof. wenigstens zu seiner Vergnügung lesen, und
vielleicht zu Magdeb. oder Halberstadt [end of page -- section 
missing???] Zeugen von der möglichkeit, daß denen der 
Gott lieben, alles zum guten mitwürcken muß
3. H. Falckners Brieff aus Pensylvanien habe nachgesandt, hoffe, 
es werde selbiger dem H. Prof. noch zu Berlin worden. Hiebey 
kommt eine Inlage daraus nach Quedlinburg gehörig, die der 
Herrn Prof. entweder selbst überreichen oder von Halberstadt 
aus sicher bestellen kan, weil ich mit der Post fast bedencken 
getragen habe, indem er ist gar weit herkommet.

4. Nach einer kommt aus Stackholm von Herr Schäffern, der 
Ziemlich lang dabey eine Inlage nach QUedlenberg welche 
gleichfalls mit kommet, zum bestellung.

5. H. Franckens briefe von Venedig so viel die Einlagen 
betrifft, sind theils hier bestellet, theils gehörn weiter 
e.g. einer nach Gothe, dazu aber aus Leipzig 20 rl zu erheben, ob
der H. Prof. selbige empfangen, oder iemanden ordre gegeben habe,
weiß ich nicht, oder ob ich den Brieff an die Fr. Mutter bis 
zu Empfang besagter ? hier behalten soll will uffen freytag 
vernehmen aus Magdeburg da Sie hoffentl. schreiben könnendes 
donnerstages.

5. H. Wirth von Nürnberg recommendirt 2 studosos

6. H. Rauner sendete jüngst an noch beylage an H. 
Kalckbörner, so hoffent. aus Magdeb. nach Meseberg 
befördet werden kan.

7. Am Samtage abends habe mit dem jungen Grafen die Wäsche 
des H. Prof. nach Halberstadt in einen briefe gesandt, mit 
addresse bey H. Hoff Rath schreiben; die Fr. PRof. läßt 
sagen, wenn vor seiner Wieder kunft nicht etwas von schwartzer 
Wäsche anhero gesandt würde, so findet Er hernach gar 
nichts weißes, es sey denn, daß von den 
Halberstädtischen nach etwas weiß bliebe

8.....
continues with latest news

Scheibell Henrich
Francke 
A H
Notes: Hochehrwürdiger und Hochgelahrter Herr 
Professor!

Nachdehme Längstens Schreiben Erwartet, daß H. Urlsperger
Nebst seinen Reyße gefährden (Worünter Mein Sohn 
Georg Scheibell Cost wohlangelanget währen, so Empfingge 
Endlichen die Nachricht bey gestricher arrivirte Post durch H. 
Hanckwitz, daß selbige an. 3tn Octobr S.N. wohl angelanget 
wahren in Halle und wie H. Urlsperger meldet Mh. Professor auf 
bereits anstalten gemachet und besagte Mein Sohn bey H. Prof. 
Michaels am Triff, p. Ein Reichstal. die woche und das Logiament 
a Zwölff Reichstal. p. annum angestellet seye benebst einen 
prsens Menschen so ein gutte Latniste so in privat anweisung thue
ordiriret habe dafür durch mich die gebührende Zahlung 
auch schon Zeitliche anstalten gemacht werden sollen und solches 
zusammen mit Hr. Godfr Harckwitz allemahl gesehen? solle Ich 
werde viele obligation dafür haben, Wen Mr. Prof. Franck 
(dessen Renommes allhier sehr gross zuweylen Notice meinest Sohns
nimbst und sich seines wohl erhaltenß öfters 
benachtragest Er hat sonsten ein guthes geüth und wird 
hoffentlich guthe unterichtung und Ermahnungen danckbarlich gerne
annohmes so alleß ja zu seines besten gesch? welches MH. 
Professor gäntzlich anheimb stelle und an Etwen statt mit 
Ihme verfahren lasse, alß mit dessen Eigenen Kinds, den es 
seine Mutter und Mich wie auch allen anverwandten Eine gross 
freude seyn wird allen gutten Report von Ihme zu hören Nach 
den sein Ingen sein nun in weniger Zeit finden werden, so kan man
hernach auß dem Pedagog fernerst procediren, Ich bin sehr 
dafür daß Er ein perfectesLateiner und daß selbe wie 
sein eigens Muttersprache Lerne und sich gleich anfangs 
gewöhne Zureden, welches Eine große Unterlaßung der 
hiesigen Medicin ist, waß sonste Für büche so für
Ihme gegenwürtig Nötig, auch allemahl für seine Purse
Jedoch moderate (mittanstalten machen werde)un Ersuche durch. 
wiewohlen MH. annoch anbekndten, viel molestire hiebey, daß 
tete hierüber einwenig mittachtung möge genommen worden 
und sich ja des alle zugroßen freyheit niciht zuviele 
Zugebrauchten sondern wo übrige Zeitdaß dem Uberlasen un 
Eremeß?? zu studieren recommendiren, nd hierzu ich hoff Er 
auch gerne die Instruction anNehmen werden wird Ubrigens stelle 
alleß MEH professor Ihres ? fürschung anher? Wie sie es 
an besten halten? Ihme auf best fürgenohmen Welches ich Jeder
Zeite danchbarlich Erkennen Und Nehmens werde, Gott 
Verharrüng Meineß hochgeEhrendens Herrn Professor,
En Dienst Ergebenster Diner
Hen. Scheibell, Apoth.
London den 7th October 1712

Notes: Hochwürdig, Hochgelärter, Besonders
Hochgeehrter Herr Dr.

Nachdeme ich vor 8 Tagen alhier Gott seye dafür Lob und Danck
gepreister glücklich und gesund retourniret bin, finde ich 
bey meiner Ankünft Dero hochgeschäetes vom 11 pass. in 
schuldigster Erwiderung dene daß das darinn gementioneirte 
Packetlein gedruckte Schriften mich zu Hamburg verfehlet hat, 
selbiges aber ist inzwischen doch durch einen Schiffer anhero 
gebracht und von mir an Herrn Crusium überwiesen worden, der 
demEmpfang so er noch nicht geschehen, nechstens advisiren wird.
Daß bewüste Geld ist seither von Mr. Clon (Clow?) 
eingegangen, deßen betrag ich auch herrn Crusio zugestelt, 
als daß hievon ein mehrer nicht zu repliciren fält, 
alß MHr für die dißfals genommen bemühung 
schuldigsten Danck zusagen. Im übrigen wird mich erfreuen 
wan Ihnen hiesiger Orten einig angenehme Dinste werde erzeigen 
können, wozu mich willen offerire und unter Empfehl. 
Göttlr. Protectn. nebst freundl. Salut. beharre
Meiner Hochgeehrtesten Herren
Dienst Ergebenster
GeorgSchütz
London an 15 7bre 1702

PS: Wo Sie occsion haven an Sir? Herrn Prediger Feüerlein 
den Jüngern zuschreiben, so ersuche unbeschwerd nebst meiner 
begrüßung zugedencken daß mit nechsten an Ihn 
schreiben und von der mir aufgetragenen Commission bericht 
erstalten werde, Bemühung bitte Zu Sousiren

Abstract: Literaturhinweis: Theodor Wotschke: August Hermann Franckes Deborah. In: Neue kirchliche Zeitschrift 1929, S. 271-272.

Schwartz ist vor einer Reise nach Erfurt gewarnt worden. Hingegen ist sie nach Quedlinburg gefahren, um die Stigmata [von A. E. Jacobs] zu sehen.
Notes: Jesus Stärke seine Seele in anliegen und 
vielfeltigern Heiligen arbeit

Mein Theuerster Bruder, seine liebe ist so reichlich in dem Herrn
an mir gewesen daß ich davon nicht wenig trostes empfunden O!
gelobet sey Gott der alles wohl machet ich bin stille zu seiner 
ewigen liebe, O! Er laße Sie flißen in unser aller Seelen
wie Sträme und sey unsere stete hoffnung die uns ergquicke in
allen leiden Welche der feindt noch in weg Wirflet, ich wartte 
von einer morgen wache biß zur anderen auff die Völlige 
erhöfnung israelis, doch findet meine Seele nie nie mehr 
Kraft, alß wenn Sie ein stetes sterben vor sich hat in dem 
Herrn. der alles Wohl machet ja dem ich dieses schreibe komt. 
H. L ? Sair und saget daß die red in Hall gehe, ob? were in 
Erfurt bestellet bey meiner ankomft mich in arest zunehmen nun 
gestehe ich daß ich anstendlich bestürtzt wurde, allein 
ich ermannte mich, in dem Herrn der je weist daß es nicht umb
übelthat sondern umb seines heiligen nahmens willen. der 
meine freund und trost ist, geschehe, darüber wurde ich 
jenigst erfreuet, und prieste die liebe Gottes und sehe auch in 
solchen sterben daß leben halleluja. ja dem kam der H. 
Oberste und Zeiget mir einen brieff von H. Hoffrath Printz darinn
eben daß vorige stund nun? denche doch mein bruder wie mich 
der Hand deß Herrn so weißlich geführet, wie ich hir 
her kam, so hilte mich der H. Oberse aus guten hertze auff, auch 
daß es so sehr raues Windigstes Wetter war und ich wurde auch
innerlich gehalten. und endlich gelenket diesen vorgangenen 
montag nach quedlinburg zu reisen da ich die Frau geseh und 
gesprochen welche von blutigen strichen immer der haut so durch 
scheinende buchstaben auff der hand hatte nehml. 3 W. und 3 + 
auch die buchstaben iHS daß sonderl. anzusehen. Sie 
verkündiget mit faßen und beten dreyer Tage buß, 
zureißet ihre kleider und stelt sich sehr übel aber die 
träßung von den leiden Jesu ist dabey. kan wegen mangel 
der Zeit nicht alles beschreiben. welche nur nach zur nötige
nachricht daß auch die freude augusta Große bewegung hat 
in den Herrn sie hat mich in Großer entzüchung oder sage 
jamerlicher erhebung und bewegung angeredet mit sehr herlichen 
worten. Sie wird morgen so Gott will und ihre 
unbößlichkeit es nicht verhindert nebst der Fr. Stifts 
Hauptmännin und H. V. Schönberg die Hertzlichst 
grüßen, von quetlburg abreisen zu euch lieben hertzen 
nach Hall, wie bey kommender brief aus weißen wird den ich 
mit ein eigen boten fortsenden wolte, aber ietzt durch H. Printz 
geschichten, sende. Morg. geliebtes Gott will ich durch H. Stiren
mehr schreiben. den liebsten H. D. Breith. grüße ich viel
1000 mahl O! Theüerste Hertze seydt gegrußet mit den 
süßen gruß deß friedes unseres Jesu dem ich euch 
erlaße und sterbe eure magd in den Herrn A. H. S. (can't 
read p.s.)

Mein hertzens bruder, ich werde so der Herr will morgen geliebtes
Gott von hir ab nach Schönigen, Halbst. und Quetlinb. reisen,
alwo ich ein briflein von dir verhoffe anzutreffen daß mir

ich nur jmmer? lauterer und ein feltiger folgen möge ich 
hette woll vieles zuschreiben aber ich verspare es aufs negste 
der Herr wird alles fügen, wie es sein solle. Fort: kanstu 
sagen von deinen gedanken, wegen eyßleben hiesige lieben 
freunde grüßen hertzl. grüße auch von mir die 
kinder gottes bey dir. sonderl. die letztens nach an mich 
geschrieben alß H. M. K. M. und die liebe jungf. W. aber ich 
kan wegen mangel der Zeit ietzt nicht antwort. weg deß 
wiederstands so dir geschichet wirds der Herr H. woll machen, 
traue seiner gätte Er weist wozu dieses oder ienes gut ist. 
es ist boßer daß es dir verbote wird, alß wenn da 
etwaßdarinn geendert hettest. nun der liebe Vatter wird alles
Wohl machen. bleibe seiner treu hertzl. besehlen?

Notes: Jesus umbfange dich mit gnad und liebe
Mein werthester bruder ich berichte dich mit diesen meinige 
zeillen, daß ich bißhie her auff gehalten worden meine 
reiß nicht fertzusetzen, bin aber nach deß Herrn Willen 
nun in gewißer hoffnung am Freytag aus Quetlenburg zufahren

einkehren kan ich gedacht an H. Sprechelsen loguiret oder gerad 
zu auff dein Hauß in H. Kirchen Stube, in der Kleidung werde 
ich eine Verenderung haben und daß gesicht mit kappen zu 
gewinckelt, daß also eyßerlich unkennlich sein werde, der
Herr H. füge alles nach seinen heiligen Rath und Willen, so 
einiche liebe hertzen von leibzig gegen wertig sein, bitte ich 
ihnen im Vertrauen solche meine ankunft zu sagen. Friede sey mit 
dir ich bin wie allezeit deine getreue schw. d.
den liebe fort: und Gamed? bitte zu grüßen
den 22 Feb. 1693

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 52
Author: Schwartz, Adelheid Sibylle
Year: 1693
Title: [Berlin?]
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1693/03/06
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 19,2/20:10 [6812]
Custom 1: 1693-03-06
Custom 2: 52.520008, 13.404954
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Notes: Jesus laß fließen neue Krafft licht heyl und 
leben
Mein werther bruder Siehe! ich bin berichtet worden, ob solte 
deine liebe Seele hie und da angestoß genommen haben, auch an
mir sein irre geworden, nun! gestehe ich daß freylich eine 
angefochtene oder bekümmerte Seel leicht hie und da gefahr 
leidet, aber mein liebes hertz du kennest ja unseren grundt, ich 
bitte dich umb der wunden Jesu willen laß dem feindt keinen 
raum, Er suchet anitzo uns zu sichten wie denn wäitzen. Ach! 
der liebste Herr Jesus wie Er damahls vor seine jünger 
gebeten hat, ach! so bete Er nach für uns, seinen heiligen 
nahmen gebühret Ehre jmmer und ewiglich. Ach! hertzens kind 
der liebste Herr Jesus siehet sich so haltseelig nach dir umb, 
und verlanget nach deiner Seelen, mit heiligen verlangen daß 
sie brünstig in ihn kehre, Siehe doch lauterlich auff seinen 
Willen, der da ist, daß wir liebe unter einander haben 
sollen. O! lieber bruder daran er kennet man die jünger 
Christi O! so bitte ich dich hertzlich laß diesem geruch von 
dir richen, wie Er wahrhaftig noch versiegelt liget in deinem 
grund aber die welt buhlet darumb, mit künstl. Verstellungen,
traue nicht, Traue nicht, mein bruder, ich will lieber die 
unvollkommenheit derer tragen, die ich weiß, daß sie vom 
Herrn ergriffen sein, und sich nach der vollendung sehnen durch 
daß lames blut, daß sie reiniget von ihrem Sünden 
alß die greuel babels, O! wie lißig ist die schlang, 
daß sie uns den schaden so verdechet, alß ob man von 
ihrer frucht nur klüger würde, O! nein! es ist betrug, 
wir muße sie fliehen. Nun! meine werthere bruder, ich 
seüftze inniglich zum Herrn für dich, daß Er dir 
kraft verleyhen wolle, ietziger Gefahr zuentrumen?, O! es ist 
noch umb ein kleines so wird die göttliche kraft zum leben je
mehr und mehr hervor brechen, were da hat dem wird gegeben 
werden, daß Er die fülle habe, O! kehre dich schnell zum 
Herrn mit jenigen verlangen, daß Er dich aus aller versuchung
und anhaltung erlösen wolle, seine treu ist unendlich glaube 
mir, daß ich es vor gott hertzlich meine, und dich woll 
erkennen kan ich habe der gleiche auch versuchet weyland, aber 
gelobet sey gott. der mein hertz hat vest gemacht an sich 
welches gemachet, daß ich alle schwachheiten der kinder 
gottes mit liebe habe tragen können, und habe nicht gesehen, 
darauff sondern auff daß gute, so ich an ihnen gefunden, und 
habe nur verlanget nach der Wahrheit die Christl. aufrichtigkeit 
in acht zu nehmen, hirinne bin ich sicher gegangen, alß ich 
in Hall war, fühlete meine Seele woll eine Verenderung an 
dir, aber ich war doch der Hoffnung daß du kraft haben 
würdest, solche anfechtungen zu überwunden, wie ich auch 
noch glaube ich hatte auch gern grundlich mit dir geredet aber 
Zeit und gelegenheit wolte es ie nicht leiden, weil es sich nicht
schicken kont, daß ich zu dir gekommen were. nun dem Herrn 
sey mein andencken der liebe Vor dich, befohlen, Er ruffe dir zu,
mit seiner göttl. stimme, fürchte dich nicht, erschrick 
nicht, jesus von nazaret hat gesieget und will auch in dir 
stegen? Halleluja Halleluja freue dich Erde lobet ihr berge mit 
jauchzen, dem der Herr hat sein Volck getrößet und 
erbarmmet sich seiner ellenden. nun! ich muß abbrechen mein
bruder, der liebste Herr Jesus nehm dich in seinen heiligen 
schutz und schirm, lebe in seiner liebe ewig wohl. so es sein kan
bitte ich umb ein par zeillen antwort. ich sterbe mein liebe 
bruder deine ins Herrn gestreuer Schwester
Adelheit Sibylla Schwartzin
den 26 Mertz 1693
die antwort kan mir H. Baumbarten wider zu gestellet werden.

Reference Type:  Unused 1

Author: Schwartz, Johann Heinrich
Year: 1694
Title: Lübeck
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1694/02/28
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 19,2/22:18 [6859]
Custom 1: 1694-02-28

Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Notes: Lübeck den 28 Febr. 1694
Immanuel!
Mein hertzgeliebter H. Mag. und im Christo sehr wehrter Bruder
Durch diese wenige Zeilen gruße Ich gar hertzl. und bericht 
daß die Schachtel und gedruckten Sachen woll an gelanget, 
auch ein jedes an seinen Ohrt befodert, die alle gebehten 
wiederumb frl. zu grüßen, und sich bedancken für 
daß übersandte, gesonderheit der H. D. Nolte, der 
gegenwärtigen brieff, gebracht, mit bitte mit ein zu 
schließen, welches ich dan habe hiemit thun wollen, weil mein
LIebes weibgen nicht zu Hauße, sondern bey dem Herrn D. 
Hattenb. auff seinen Gut, und Ihre Beyde kleinsten kinder bey 
sich hat, umb in abwesenheit des H. D. zuzusehen, der heute in 
Nahmen des Herrn seiner reise an trit, hinauff nach seinen H. 
Vatter den Er sambt seiner Fr. und 2 Kindern und 1 Mädgen 
daß Ihren dient denselben besuchen sirdt. ohne Zweiffle wird 
er auch auf Halle zusprechen, da Er dan von hiesigen Zustandt 
berichten wird, Im übrigen leben wir den Herrn sey Danck noch
wohl und Kehren umb an allen Streit und Zwanck, läster und 
verlaundung nichts, den der Herr stehet uns bey, und hat uns 
bißhieher außgeholffen Er wirdts ferner thun Ihrer sey 
Ehre immer und Ewigl. amen. Halleluja. Weg des Jung Gloxin wird
der H. D. Nolto in gegenwertigen woll geschrieben haben. Er hat 
bey mir vorgestern angefangen zu Zeichnen alle Tage eine Stunde 
welches die vormunder verlangen 4 Stunde gehet Er bey einen 
Studios. 1 stunde zum schreib. und Rechen meister und 1 stund zu 
mir alle Tage, Waß nun auß Ihm werden wird, weiß der 
Liebe Gott. H. D. Nolto sagt ja, daß Er gar nicht wieder 
nach Halle wolle, sonsten bey mir gangen, habe also noch nicht an
Ihm kommen können, der vertraulichkeit, die Er vor her zu uns
hatte, da er vor Halle kam, die ist nicht mehr da sonsten alles 
frembd, tantzen wie ich Höre soll Er auch lernen, welches Er 
auch Thun würde Ach! der Herr Erbarme sich der armen Seelen 
umb Christi willen amen. im Hauße und am tisch ist Er bey H.
P. Stein. Deßen bruder der ein Doct. Medi ist auch alda, auch
hat Er einen Stud. bey seinen kindern, da Er ja Hoffentlich 
nichts böses sehen und hören wirdt, nun waß solll man
sagen der Herr laße alles zum besten gereichen die hiesieg 
freunde alle laßen gar hertzl. Grüßen, welche Ich 
auch thue und Hoffe meine Liebste wirdt bald selbermehr 
schreiben, Ich bin nur einschlechte schreiber und habe auch der 
Zeit nicht nun mein bruder so nehme Er mit mir verlieb Ich habe 
mir diße brief fortsenden wollen Im übrigen gruße ich
noch zum dritten mahl und befehle Ihn der samften liebe Jesu und 
bleibe sein getrewer b ruder in den herrn J. H. Schwartz

PS: von deren streitigkeiten so in Hamburg Zwischen H. D. 
Hinckelen und H. D. Mayer vergangene werden Sie ja woll 
gehöret haben. H. Horbius wil nun baldt gantz weg gehen nach 
Berlin der H. Gott geleite Ihn
Von der hiesig großen waser flut so viel schaden gethan 
werden sie auch woll gehöret haben.

Author: Schwartz, Johann Heinrich

Title: Berlin
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1703/02/04
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 19,2/22:17 [6858]
Custom 1: 1703-02-04

Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]

Notes: Gott mit Uns!
Indensleben hertzgeliebter H. Professor sehr wehrter lieber 
Gönner

Seine große Liebe und trewe, so der Hertzgeliebte freund, in 
seinen Brieffe, nicht nur allein mit worten, sondern auch in der 
That an Uns Erwiesen, mit einem solchen helden Glauben, und 
vertrawen auff den Lebendigen Gott, die müße Ewiglich 
geseegnet und verherlicht werden, vor dem Angesicht deßen, 
der alle ding erschaffen, und seinen Heiligen und Außer 
wehlten, an jenem tage wen alles wird Offenbahr werden. Waß 
sollen wir sagen, der Herr hats gethan, der des L. Freundes Hertz
hat willig gemacht, auch daß vermögen dazu gegeben, 
worumb Ich und meiner L. Fraw, wohl hertzlich geseuffzet, u. 
gebehtet haben. dem Herrn sey Lob, Preiß und danck fur seine
große Gnade, und dem Lieben H. Profess. für sein liebes 
und gut williges Hertz. Es ist mit der Außzahlung an die 
Hall Jungster gantz gut abgangen, daß Sie nicht gemerckt, wir
werden die Order der verschweigenheit, auch vertrautesten, durch 
Hülf des Herrn treulich nachkommen, Meine L. Fraw hette gern 
selbst geschrieben, ist aber noch zu Matt, wie wohl sie durch die
Gnad des Lieben Gottes ein wenig in der Beßerung ist, diesen 
Sprüch sagt Sie soll ich schreiben. der Gerechte wirt LEben 
und sein Same wirt fur Ihme gedeyen, der Herr wolle unsern 
Glauben stärcken und besfestigen durch seine Almachtige 
Kraft, wan die wirt in uns wircken, werden wir treülich an 
diese liebe gedencken, nun bey dem Herrn ist kein ding 
unmöglich. Indeßen gnad und liebe, ich den wehrten H. 
prof. sambt allen leiben angehorigen getreulich empfehle, nebst 
gar jeniglichen gruß von mir und meine L. frawen verbleibe 
meines theuren H. Prof. und hertzgeliebten freundes Ewig 
verbundener diener
Johann Heinrich Schwartz
Berlin den 4 Feb. 1703
Alle alle freuend mit nahmen grußen wir in herrn hertzlich

Reference Type:  Unused 1
Record Number: 148
Author: Schwartz, Johann Heinrich
Year: 1703
Title: Berlin
Secondary Author: Francke, August Hermann
Secondary Title: [Halle]
Publisher: Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin
Date: 1703/06/10
Type of Work: letter
Short Title: Francke-Nachlaß, 19,2/22:20
Custom 1: 1703-06-10
Custom 2: 52.520008, 13.404954
Custom 3: [51.496979, 11.968803]
Notes: Berl. den 10 Juny 1703
Immanuel!
Indenselben Teurester Freund und Hertz geliebter Bruder

Sein geliebtes Brieffgen, von 2 Juny habe den 7dito wohl 
erhalten, und ist solcher Brieff ein erquickender Balsam, meinen 
Armen hertzen gewesen, wofur der Nahme des Herrn gelobet sey, 
durch den Brieff des H. Dobbelers wurde mein hertz gar matt, ja 
fast verzagt gemacht, konte mich auch weder rathen noch helffen, 
da da mein wehr und waffen gewesen und noch ist, behten, weinen 
und flehen, der liebe Vatter der ja uns verbargene siehet, wird 
sich ja umb CHristi willen meiner Erbarmen, und aus helffen, 
nicht nach meiner, sondern nach seinen gnädigen willen, meine
Liebe sehlige Frau sagte ofter vor Ihren Ende, Mein liebes Kind, 
wo Ich sterbe, so mußen dich an einer Freund offenbahren, der
Herr wird dier Helffen, und einen solchen Zeigen Ich habe nach 
Ihren Absterben Ofte daran gedacht bald an dießen und jenen, 
es hat sich aber nichts fügen wollen, biß der liebe 
bruder nun selbst sich dau an erbietet, also Zweiffele auch nicht
der Herr wirt Ihm auch kraft und stärcke dazu innerlich und 
Eüsterlich geistlich und leiblich mit voller Maße geben, 
waß nun meine umbstände anlanget, so habe noch nicht 
alles aufgeschrieben waß an Mobilien als betten, leinen sins 
und Meßing habe ich will aber sehen ein rechter INventarium 
zu machen, nur muß daß berichten, daß weil ich auf 
Johannes als nach 14 Tage auß diesen Hauße ziehen werde, 
daß cih meinte etwas an große Schrancke und bettstede zu 
verkauffen, weil ich 1 1-2 Jahr miete schuldig bin, daß bey 
100 Thaler sein wirt und wohl nicht weiß, wo ich rathen soll 
wen ich nicht, waß verkaufte, umb solches Abzutragen, und 
darff auch nicht Ehe aus ziehen biß solche miete bezahlet 
habe die andern Creditoren können und werden noch wohl 
warten, waß nun meine Nahrung anlanget, so ist es etwas 
schlecht, wolte mir der Liebe Gott andere Arbeit geben wäre 
Ich auch zu frieden, doch meine, weil meine haußhaltung 
kleiner wirt, durch den Seegen und Hilffe des Herrn, etwas zu 
verdienen, wie wohl meine Augen abnehmen, den Ich schon ins 50 
Jahr meines alters gehe, waß die Kinder betrift so wirt die 
Alste Tochter Adeheit Sib. zu H. Doct. Petersen kommen, der Alste
Sohn wolte sehen ab Ihm hier bey etlichen freunden die woche ein 
mahl ein Tisch bekommen könte, der Kleinste sohn ist gar ein 
hurtigen knabe, und sehr scharfen verstandes und große last 
zu den buchern, der herr woll e Zeigen, wozu Er ihn versehen hat,
der Mitteste Sohn ist meinen Profession der mir schon helfen kan,
und daß Mittelste Madgen wolte bey mir behalten, wo es den 
Hern Gefiehle, der es noch seiner heil gut und gnade Ordnen und 
fügen wolle zu seiner Ehre und meinen Ewigen heylm weil aber 
Itz die Zeit zu kurtz alß wil mit hulffe Gottes Kunftig Post 
mehr schreiben, und die Nahmen benennen, an wehm all schuldig bin
dieß mahl habe mir gegen wartig brieff bey der ersten Post 
senden wollen bitte es nicht übel zu deuten Ich bruße von
grund des hertzens und bleibe negst empfhelung der Gnaden Gottes 
meines wehrten bruder dinestwilligst diener
Johann Hein Schwartz
ps: die Wehrte Fr Liebste wie auch die lieben kinder gruße 
ich und meine Kinder hertzl. bedancke mich auch fur daß 
briefgen so dir Fr. Liebste geschrieben
